letter policy and politics at the labour party conference
from mr denis macshane
sir if labour is to suggest the setting up of a specialist labour court september then such a momentous change in the industrial relation system deserves more discussion and need to be taken out of the of labour party conference politics
for three reason such a move should be welcomed
first it would bring britain into line with the best european practice notably in germany where local regional and federal labour court handle problem in a fair dispassionate way based on law precedent and judicial expertise in the labour field
second it would ensure that worker enjoyed positive right under law and reduce the emphasis of union immunity
labour law will always reflect the balance of power in society and a fully fledged labour court system will not remove class and fundamental difference
but it should be possible to create and enforce enough common rule to prevent the absurd of industrial relation legislation we have seen since
third a labour division of the high court would contribute to the process of constitutional reform in britain which surely is to be a key political issue in the
the trade union question would cease to haunt the labour party and while that might upset some conservative it would be good for the country

latecomer who continue to hope
from anne applebaum in warsaw
dozen more east german refugee arrived outside the west german embassy yesterday seeking asylum and passage to the west including some who missed by only a few minute a train that took more than of their compatriot to west germany

the east german government decision to let the refugee leave across their own country came a a surprise to many including some west german diplomat
some of the refugee originally refused to touch east german territory again but were reassured when two of the west german diplomat said they would accompany the train to ensure that the rule were followed
during the journey east german official will enter the train and collect all east german passport
west german will then issue new one
legally the refugee have been expelled from east germany meaning that under current rule they can not return
according to unofficial report the arrangement wa designed by the west german foreign minister han dietrich genscher the new polish foreign minister krzystof skubiszewski and the soviet foreign minister eduard shevardnadze who met recently at the united nation in new york
communist allow burial of montenegro last king
from marcus tanner in cetinje yugoslavia
the people of montenegro yesterday welcomed home the remains of nicholas i their first and last king after year exile in italy in belated fulfilment of his last will and testament
thousand of montenegrins many in national costume waited at the quayside in bar for the italian warship that would bring him home
then they formed a slow procession behind the coffin into the mountain to the old royal capital of cetinje for his reburial in the monastery there
what wa surely the last ever montenegrin royal event wa masterminded by the republic new communist leadership which ha abruptly stopped describing nicholas a a class enemy to ride the same wave of popular patriotism and royal fervour which swept serbia in the recent celebration of the anniversary of the battle of kosovo
the latest biography now call him an outstanding statesman warrior and man of letter
if i die abroad in exile let my body rest in a temporary grave until my mortal remains be transferred to our dear homeland said the montenegrin president branko kostic reading the royal will and testament to the crowd in cetinje square who carried flag and portrait of nicholas and his queen milena
today the people of montenegro fulfill the wish of their first and last king guided by innate love and respect for their history he went on
our tourist organisation are counting on big profit said srdan darmanovic a member of the montenegrin central committee
this will be good for the montenegrin economy too
montenegro young and leadership which came to power this year amid furious popular dissatisfaction with the old men in grey suit sponsored the gathering of nicholas surviving relative the first royal reunion organised by a communist government
a letter dropped through the post from the president of the socialist republic of montenegro inviting me to the funeral said john kennedy a conservative party member who life in barking and is a distant relative of nicholas
montenegro sudden rehabilitation of nicholas memory is a popular move
he liberated u from the turk and fought for our independence said a small boy who waited at the quayside amid a jostling crowd of former monarch visiting serbian bishop and television crew
marko radoman and a veteran of both balkan war wa given a place at the front a one of the few with personal memory of nicholas reign
for a man whom rebecca west a contemporary balkan observer called repulsive and treacherous for deserting his serbian king alexander in the first world war it is a view of history
nicholas wa known a the uncle of europe for his success in marrying his beautiful but penniless daughter into the grander royal house of russia serbia and italy
this furthered his ambition to rule a large south slav kingdom when the ottoman empire finally collapsed
one daughter a grand duchess of russia even gained a footnote in history by introducing an unknown monk rasputin to the russian tsarina alexandra
in his minute inaccessible capital which today ha only inhabitant nicholas erected a miniature european court and an exquisitely furnished victorian palace
he even persuaded european power to turn cottage into full embassy
it wa a fair achievement in a town which an earlier observer described a hovel
but nicholas grand design collapsed in when his serbian alexander deposed him and incorporated montenegro into yugoslavia
obituary virgil thomson
by peter dickinson
virgil thomson wa a composer and writer of originality courage and wit formed by a unique mixture of american and french influence
thomson wa born in kansa city in studied at harvard and then mostly lived in paris until
his missouri childhood gave him access to baptist hymn and church music but at harvard he wa introduced to the writing of gertrude stein and the music of erik satie
these influence laid the foundation for the blend of the naive and the sophisticated which is the hallmark of thomson maturity
like many young american composer he studied with nadia boulanger but after set out to achieve the discipline of spontaneity which he found in stein writing
when he collaborated directly with her in opera the result wa of historical significance
first came four saint in three act produced in and then the mother of u all which demonstrated a new kind of plotless opera only now reaching a wider currency through the stage work of philip glass
in four saint thomson informality wa given free reign since he first of all improvised the music at the piano then when it stuck wrote it down to a figured bass
he said i had wondered whether a piece so drenched in anglican chant running from gilbert and sullivan to morning prayer and back could rise and sail
but the resulting mixture of hymn folksy tune and recitative at time of intoxicating banality wa a sensation
the opera like gershwin porgy and be the following year used an cast and the staging and choreography gave it a british connection since it wa by frederick ashton
the mother of u all show more continuity but again much depends upon production in what is still a largely opera
in three year before aaron copland thomson started writing film score which were a model of unobtrusive clarity and pertinence combining american material to suit documentary such a the plow that broke the plain and the river with the musique approach of satie
his score for the film louisiana story wa awarded the pulitzer prize in
another response to a visual stimulus wa thomson series of musical portrait of people such a picasso and aaron copland
the first of these wa written in and they number about
just a thomson transferred stein literary abstraction to music so these portrait unusually employ the painter technique of drawing the sitter from life an ideal combination of thomson habit of immediate response with an actual subject
the result are terse and sharply etched like the best line drawing
thomson could control word with the same fastidiousness a note
he always felt that effective musical criticism began by being well written and he never lost his liveliness
one never quite knew what he wa going to say next
he started by writing occasional article but in he wrote the state of music a trenchant and provocative assessment of the machinery of the musical profession at the time
from to he wrote regularly for the new york herald tribune and four volume of his notice have appeared in book form
he wrote a fulsome autobiography characteristically entitled virgil thomson on virgil thomson and a personal survey american music since appeared in followed recently by a selected edition of his letter
a both composer and critic he touched both side of the coin a climate of receptivity is what the artist most desire
it is also a thing that even the most experienced reviewer can not always offer
thomson judgement about music were not always a accurate a his confident expression implied he invited discussion
above all he restored the focus of music criticism onto the music itself
he made no secret of his francophile enthusiasm in reaction to the earlier domination of american music by german and he wa one of the first writer to register the importance of jazz
he fearlessly attacked convention which caused problem when he pitched into established reputation
it ha become increasingly apparent that thomson belonged to the american experimental tradition
he anticipated some of the enthusiasm of john cage whom he first met in
a few year later thomson recognised cage a the most original composer in america if not the world and cage repaid the compliment by writing the work section of a monograph on thomson
but finally in spite of their common root in satie and stein thomson felt that cage aesthetic wa destructive
thomson song contain some of his finest work
there are stein setting such a portrait of fb but also cycle such a five song from william blake prayer and praise and a cantata based on poem by edward lear
thomson wa also prolific in instrumental music on both chamber and solo scale
for many year thomson lived in new york in his apartment at the chelsea hotel
from there like a buzzard in it eyrie he would make foray round the u and abroad in spite of his advanced age
he seemed a genial and indestructible landmark in the history of american music in spite of defective hearing which had bothered him since the late seventy
he had a photograph of himself on his postcard and he signed his letter following the original tailpiece everbest
thomson came from a generation of american composer which had to find it own way without benefit of university patronage
in that kind of free market he thrived and survived and so will the best of his work
obituary thomas keller
by hugh matheson
thomi keller is the outstanding figure in the history of international rowing
he wa president of fisa federation internationale de societes the world governing body for year and most of this body attitude and practice reflect the force of his strict but genial personality
most athlete first encountered him a a voice bellowing in fury at official who had broken rule or arrangement designed to make racing safer or more fair
he wa elected to succeed gaston mullegg a president of fisa when he wa and still competing in the swiss rowing team
he did not loosen his link with the athlete when projected upwards into the presidency
provided their behaviour wa sportsmanlike and safe oarsman found only encouragement and humour from a president who wa always among them
keller zurich upbringing made him into a skiier and sculler and he raced for the grasshopper club
he competed for the swiss and team at the student winter game and later concentrated on single scull
in he wa swiss scull champion and finished third in the european championship before moving to manila to work for his family private multinational company eduard keller ltd for four year
on his return keller wa swiss champion again in and wa bitterly disappointed when the swiss chose to boycott the olympics after the russian intervention in hungary
fisa wa then a relatively unimportant body which organised european and other championship and participated in the running of olympic regatta
a a rich forceful young man keller had been earmarked a a likely future president even before mullegg wa killed in an aircrash in
rowing wa transformed in the breadth and depth of participation over the year of his term
he sat on the appropriate board of the international olympic committee and wa president of the general assembly of international sport federation for year
these position were not held for his own status but to promote the cause of rowing where it needed clout
he successfully defended rowing a an olympic sport and in introduced woman event which have now expanded to six class
his personal preference for sculling over rowing assisted the introduction of quadruple scull to world championship and olympic competition
keller wa made a steward of henley royal regatta in a time when the proliferation of new course around the world which had emerged under his guidance seemed a threat to the regatta founded in
but it wa the spirit of henley with huge crowd enjoying amateur sport presented with administrative finesse which keller took a the yardstick for the international circuit
he loved the place and he returned every year to play an often small part a umpire of race between undistinguished club far below the olympic standard he wa obliged to administer
he said this summer that a he gradually wound down his involvement in sport henley would be the last thing he would give up
during his term a president of fisa he gradually reduced his role in eduard keller ltd and used the company office to provide a world headquarters for rowing
the sport is now obliged to find income from the more normal source of television and sponsorship to replace his largely unacknowledged private patronage
in spite of his gift to the sport keller wa anxious not to abuse his status a president and never went to a rowing event unless invited
because of this he had never seen the oxford and cambridge boat race until this year
he wa enthralled by the entire proceeding and remarked that only the english could make a contest between two crew which would not rank in the world top into a bigger spectacle than the olympic final
the final task he set himself for his presidency which wa due to end next year wa to weed out of the regatta calendar all the rowing course which could be made unfair by the wind
he had recently travelled from tasmania to norway in search of the perfect metre of flat water
it wa a blessing that in response to congratulation on the superb world championship regatta at bled in yugoslavia three week ago he wa able to reply yes and best of all the condition were fair throughout
the labour party conference cook appeal for labour to accept electoral reform
by colin hughes and colin brown
an impassioned appeal for labour to back electoral reform wa made by a leading shadow cabinet member yesterday after the national executive decided overwhelmingly to oppose a proportional representation motion
robin cook a member of the national executive and the health spokesman said that a labour government which sought to force it programme on an unwilling nation would be unsocialist
he told a labour committee rally that it wa not enough for labour to win the next election
it would also be necessary to smash the decrepit effete constitution that allows a minority to capture power and then use it ruthlessly in the interest of the privileged few
mr cook argued that year of thatcherism had been forced on most people who had never voted conservative and that many of those who opposed pr in the labour party wanted to use the same undemocratic power to ram socialism down the throat of a majority who did vote for it
advocate of the system argued that it wa the only way of delivering strong government mr cook said
but after year of tory rule he had had enough of that approach to politics
labour would be acquiescing in a democratic outrage if it continued arguing that because the conservative had got away with being undemocratic for so long it wa now labour turn
mr cook also countered the argument that pr would build in a pull towards the centre ground preventing labour from implementing a radical programme
it seemed strange to make that argument mr cook said when it wa clear the whole policy review process wa designed to placate the centre ground
i can not honestly see that a system which would require u to compromise the morning after the election is really so morally inferior to a system which ha already obliged u to compromise our policy two year before polling day
his speech however came aftera vote in the national executive to oppose a proportional representation motion which will be debated on thursday
the four were mr cook ken livingstone john evans and clare short
mr livingstone said he wa against pact but year of thatcherism had demonstrated the danger of giving power to elite
however neil kinnock the labour leader and roy hattersley his deputy both opposed the motion
mr hattersley said giving disproportionate power to small minority centre party would not improve democracy
mr kinnock said it wa wrong to propose a fundamental change in the voting system for a tactical vote to get rid of the thatcher government
the only way to remove the government wa for labour to win the next general election
mr kinnock intends to reinforce his conviction that labour is in a position to win in his keynote speech tomorrow
party organiser want the conference to show that the party is united a never before leaving mr kinnock free for the first time to sell the policy package to voter without worrying about split
there is expected to be a close vote on defence but mr kinnock is confident the new policy will be affirmed today
the executive is recommending rejection of a motion calling for unilateral disarmament
it is also urging the conference to oppose a motion supported by the national union of mineworker to commit a labour government to abolishing all nuclear power within year
there could also be controversy over the executive rejection of demand for the age of consent for homosexual to be reduced to year

these day no one question the importance of good book for the
but book that appeal to adult too are just a important we are after all the one who have to do the reading

should be one of the great joy of parenthood a real meeting of adult and child mind
with the ahlbergs book it very often is
the partnership behind such classic a the jolly postman burglar bill and the baby catalogue win child over with ripping yarn and a wicked sense of humour
they win their parent over with a vision of the world which is decidedly reassuring
their book are usually set nostalgically in the past the thirty and forty are favourite period and often feature the perennial character of fairy tale and nursery rhyme
yet they are saved from sentimentality by the wry humour of both text and picture
the ahlbergs have been accused of not facing up to the harsh reality of life of being too cosy and sweet but their latest picture book bye bye baby published today break the mould
in it a small child roams the street talking to stranger until he finally go off with a woman who ha been wandering about pushing an empty pram
curious subject matter for a child picture book you might think and hardly guaranteed to win the approval of the child book world
but the ahlbergs have no time for literal interpretation of their work
how they argue would alice or the wind in the willow stand up against such scrutiny
the way to look at bye bye baby they insist is a a light surreal comedy
certainly if you bring a literal interpretation to the story it a minefield allan ahlberg say
bye bye baby get away with it particular minefield thanks to the sleight of illustrator janet ahlberg hand
the visual inspiration for the book wa the famous advert for shoe showing a small boy and girl walking off down a avenue an innocent image if ever there wa one
the ahlberg version feature a solitary figure
the advert gave the story it vaguely thirty setting
the success of the ahlbergs working relationship must have a lot to do with their long and happy marriage
in spite of apparently incompatible personality she is small and shy he is large and doe most of the talking they have an empathy which is essential to the way they work a persistent mutual pestering
the strength of the partnership is highlighted for allan who also work with a number of other artist
the nature of janet part in the process combined with a bad back which prevents her spending more than a couple of hour at the drawing board every day mean she can not keep up with her husband prolific output
with other illustrator i work at a distance we visit and phone but there is a point at which i ca pester them any more allan say
they see themselves not a author and illustrator with separate role but a a partnership of contributing equally to the process
allan ahlberg say in the past a lot of child book seemed to be the work of talented illustrator whose picture looked brilliant framed in a gallery but when you tried to read the book there wa nothing there because the word started a a to hang picture on
given the importance they place on the interrelationship of word and picture the couple working life are surprisingly separate

allan experience a a primary school teacher is another rich source of idea
the couple still maintain close link with local school where they spend hour researching sketching and absorbing joke
after year of teaching allan had had enough

the revolution the countryside need christian wolmar say britain is lagging behind in setting up telecottages
by christian wolmar
the information technology revolution ha left large swath of rural britain untouched
the only computer in many village are those owned by the teenage boy of the affluent to play their game
ashley dobbs an engaging young entrepreneur is setting out to change that by creating a nationwide network of telecottages
this clever name with it neat evocation of new and old describes a concept which wa developed in sweden and is spreading to rural area across the world
in mr dobbs word a telecottage is a room in a village filled with computer communication that can be used by local people to learn and work
the equipment consists of perhaps four word processor a modem a laser printer able to produce output a fax and a photocopier
software programme for publishing word processing accounting and business planning are also essential
mr dobbs who is chairman of telecottages uk warns possible user not to get bogged down with the technology the equipment is a tool to overcome what need to be done

he reckons there are no shortage of possible us farmer can use it to do their account woman with responsibility can work in their own time on the word processor publicity material for local craftsman can be produced and so on
this may sound utopian but it ha been borne out by the experience of existing telecottages
so far about have been established mainly in scandinavia but also in japan and several third world country
a the network expands so do the us
the first wa opened in the village of vemdalen in the remote forest of sweden in september
the impact according to henning albrechsten president of telecottages international who ha been involved in their development since the outset wa immediate

britain is lagging behind
no telecottages have been established but there are several initiative in the offing
the most advanced is a plan for five in the north of scotland which will be funded by the highland and island development board and british telecom
colin pavey of british telecom hope that they will be running by the end of the year

telephone cable in the region are being upgraded to ensure they are capable of handling fax

while telecottages should become once established they do need initial subsidy
the cost of providing the equipment is in the order of and mr dobbs think space is not much of a problem there usually the village hall or an empty shop
henning albrechsten reckons that it take three year for a telecottage to be able to function without subsidy
in scandinavia with their mixed economy money is always available after a bit of persuasion from both local and central government
in britain the tight financial regime imposed on local council and the reluctance of central government to take on any new expenditure make it necessary to seek fund from the private sector
the only government support so far ha been a recommendation by the rural development commission part of the department of the environment to establish a pilot scheme
mr dobbs sigh this is a typically british bureaucratic response
it been proved elsewhere that they work
we do need pilot we need telecottages
a for the private sector while bt may be happy to provide pump priming for five telecottages in the north of scotland it is not about to bankroll a nationwide network
nor it seems is anyone else
there is more at stake here than just bringing box of sophisticated equipment to remote area
a mr dobbs who run a country house restoration business from his home in micheldever hampshire say village are good place to live and work
the village is a fantastic institution and they make people happier
but the village are dying becoming suburb or dormitory where few people work but many sleep
employment in agriculture still the main rural industry fell from over a million in the to under now
the aim of telecottages is to create flexible employment which will provide new job and make existing rural industry more competitive
the emphasis on high wage is important
village are expensive to live in and if they are to become vibrant community again local people must be able to earn enough to be able to continue living in them
there is a wider impact too
the abstract talk of commuting by rail or road being replaced by information technology find a concrete expression in the idea of telecottages
once people overcome their fear about computer and begin to use them in telecottages they acquire their own equipment
many may eventually be able to work from home rather than commute to an office
henning albrechsten say modern information technology ha given people in remote region the opportunity to overcome their worst handicap their distance from the centre of learning and development
he see them a not only strengthening small community but also a actually beginning to reverse the population flow from the countryside to the town
britain with it growing traffic problem seems an ideal place for the onset of this revolution
despite mr dobbs tireless effort this is another revolution which britain is likely to be viewing from the sideline

by james ruppert
from this month all new car submitted for british type approval the test which allows them to be legally sold in the uk must be able to run on petrol
a a result of this rule and many carefully orchestrated publicity campaign the motor industry image ha now changed from polluter to pal of the earth
if you can afford an environmentally friendly runabout then the flora fauna and child of the british isle will have a lot to thank you for
but if you have a tight budget and a conscience running older car on fuel becomes a much more complicated issue
without the presence of a lead compound an engine valve seat go unprotected
this lead to premature wear and plume of blue smoke spewing from the exhaust
the only effective remedy is to install hardened valve seat or a replacement cylinder head both expensive option
le costly but not entirely satisfactory is the practice of making every fourth tankful leaded petrol which protects the valve seat but rather defeat the object
alternatively there are several chemical additive on the market which aim to provide a substitute for lead although the case for these product ha yet to be proved
however many car built within the last few year have hardened valve seat or alloy cylinder head that need little simply a retune or no modification to use unleaded petrol
finding out which car can and which can not is not difficult
esso filling station have a free booklet listing most model produced since a doe the charity clear with more detail available in the unleaded petrol guide autodale

what is certain is that the range all skodas yugos and quite a few lancias do not which doe not help already depressed resale price
a lancia lead only sell for around whereas the similar fiat uno from the same year converted to run on unleaded is worth around more
a car is now worth about per cent le than an unleaded equivalent
in year to come the percentage difference is likely to be much larger
even so exotica such a porsche and ferraris are unlikely to be part of this trend so no bargain there i afraid
more impressive are the japanese manufacturer whose car dating from the early eighty can run on unleaded without adjustment
find a toyota corolla or nissan sunny that ha not succumbed to rust and you can buy with confidence
on the home front most ford and vauxhalls from at least the can use unleaded
if the greenness of going unleaded still seems a bit of a grey area it is possible to switch to diesel without a shadow of environmental doubt
diesel always ha been and the only adjustment you need to make are mental one because car are no longer slow smelly or noisy
they also return more mile to the gallon than their petrol equivalent although service interval are shorter
but after the publicity on unleaded fuel there ha been increased interest in used diesel power
but remember that these car accrue and can withstand significantly higher mileage than petrol car being the norm
the tradition for diesel car is far better established on the continent and that is where the best buy come from
perhaps the most successful maker is peugeot with a complete range of car from the small around for a car to the legendary estate about for a example
the german are also fairly accomplished manufacturer although a golf with a mileage will still cost
prestige come in the shape of a mercedes with the or stuttgart taxi commanding but returning unfailing reliability

in the garden planning to beat a leafy retreat at home in the first of a series for novice gardener anna pavord stress the value of careful forethought
by anna pavord
plant should come a long way down the list of priority for the novice gardener
there are many thing to think about before even the first tentative daffodil bulb is sunk into the ground
the first and most important question to mull over a you gaze at your patch is what is this garden for
if you start writing down some of the response to that question you will find you have along the way acquired a ragbag of element that will have an important bearing on the design
if there are small child in the equation there will need to be a flat soft area where they can fall off swing and climbing frame
if you like hanging out washing rather than drying it in the bowel of an expensive machine you will need to tuck away a line and make a dry path to get to and from it
some novice gardener may not want to do much actual gardening at all but conversely do not want to look out every day over a scene of threadbare grass and rotting fence
their ideal garden will look good and demand little attention
if you are a dedicated you need to mark out the part of the garden where the sun lingers longest
it may not be the part nearest the house though this is where sitting out area always tend to be made
you may even a a novice care so passionately about plant that all you want is the maximum space to grow them in
raised bed built down an unpromising alley could provide extra gardening space
privacy is an important consideration
a first time garden is usually small and certainly the typical one i am imagining for this series is no more than x and surrounded on all side by other house
privacy is a ticklish business where close neighbour are concerned
to throw up an impenetrable berlin wall between you and them could be tactless
trellis is a useful compromise and you can always pretend it wa forced on you by the speed of growth of your climbing rose
aesthete among the novice will by now be thoroughly irritable and complaining that garden should have a much to do with the soul a with the necessity or not of a washing line or a barbecue pit
so they should and when the list of necessity is securely written down you can ask the second question how do i want this garden to feel
this question produce a varied a response a the first
some urban gardener a short of space inside a they are out want their garden to be extension of their home with a great deal of hard paving good furniture and lighting
the garden for them should feel like an extra sitting room perhaps damp occasionally but an important overflow of living space
closet countrysiders may want to pretend their patch is actually a corner of some sussex meadow and picture it swagged with honeysuckle and waving with daisy and scabious
this is a difficult trick to bring off with suburban train hurtling by on one side and lorry grinding through their gear on the other
a leafy retreat is an excellent goal for a small town garden but it is best made acknowledging the urban setting using plant such a bamboo acanthus fig vine alchemilla euphorbia wisteria
while you are working through this process take note of the feature in the garden that you would like to keep
on a new estate there may be nothing
in an old garden there may be a fruit tree or a good bulwark of evergreen laurel or box that tidied up could add a dash of venerability to the new garden that will emerge around it
if you do not know what a tree or shrub is exercise clemency and give it a year grace to demonstrate it worth before you turn it over to the axeman
the mood of the garden will dictate it eventual style
it may be clipped classical random cottage modern or some intensely personal vision of byzantium that no one ha ever imagined before but which exists in your head and want to get out
do not let anybody particularly gardening writer tread on your dream
all this thinking and doodling will have done nothing physically to change the view outside the window but it is a vital part of the gardening process
before you can make you have to know what it is you are making

by andrew bibby
in the small devon town of south molton julie widlake is waiting with anticipation for friday october

it come under the hammer at on the at the barnstaple motel
we accept that we might not get very much for it but on the other hand we could get more say julie widlake
we been waiting to move for a long time and we need the money to build the new house
their south molton cottage guide price is one of more than lot to be put up for sale at the barnstaple auction by bristol and west property service and one of more than a hundred which the building society subsidiary will be auctioning in eight west country venue over a period
bristol and west claim these auction will help to bring some action to an otherwise slow market and say it wa overwhelmed by the response from people wanting to sell in this way
auction certainly speed up the process
once the hammer ha fallen the successful bidder for a house must exchange contract immediately and pay a deposit
completion normally take place four to eight week later and there is no opportunity for second thought
a the bristol and west explains if a bidder doe not sign the contract the auctioneer can sign on their behalf
from the vendor point of view the house is actually sold once a successful bid is made say graham harrison director of bristol and west property service

from the purchaser point of view auction can also be attractive if slightly a you wait for bidding to start for the house of your dream
the problem is that normally potential purchaser have to incur the expense of undertaking survey and arranging mortgage finance without any idea whether they will be able to afford the final selling price
not surprisingly several estate agent report difficulty at the moment in attracting enough serious bidder
with an auction you got to be certain that at least two buyer are there who can commit themselves and the difficulty is that buyer who can proceed are few and far between said david phillip a director of yorkshire estate agent dacre son and hartley
bristol and west hope that by arranging collective auction it will be able to overcome this problem
it is also guaranteeing mortgage at per cent below the normal interest rate for endowment or policy on several of the house up for sale an interesting and innovative service for bidder mortgage survey will already have been undertaken for these house
the building society will be staffing a mortgage desk at each auction and say buyer could arrange finance there and then subject of course to proof of income and status
obviously however bristol and west hope to hear from interested people in advance if only so it can gauge the likely demand for each property before the auction start
we trying to smooth the path for purchaser and streamline the system say graham harrison pointing out that live telephone bidding will also be available for those unable to attend
holiday home and commercial property have been included among the lot to be auctioned
although collective property auction take place regularly in london often primarily for investor rather than in country area the more typical auction will be just for one house and a likely a not will take place in a nearby pub or village hall
in fact country auction are often the nearest many village get to live theatre
the local come for the entertainment and to see who buying into their village observed one
pub landlord are usually only too happy to provide free accommodation
it very exciting and get the adrenalin going say david phillip whose firm usually undertakes auction in the otley area
only certain type of property normally come to auction however
traditionally country cottage and house which have unusual or unique feature or are in need of a lot of renovation may be auctioned if only because valuation is likely to be difficult
sometimes too house have to be sold by auction to satisfy the legal requirement of trustee or executor auction provide adequate proof that the property ha been sold at the going market value and protect trustee from future claim of negligence
le happily but for the same reason repossessed house are often auctioned
anyone considering selling by auction need to be aware that the cost involved will be higher
advertising cost and any expense incurred in hiring premise are normally passed on by the estate agent to the vendor whether or not the auction result in a sale
in addition agent may charge slightly more commission than usual for a successful sale
in bristol and west forthcoming auction a set fee of plus vat will be charged to everyone entering property to sell with it usual agent commission about per cent plus vat charged on top when sale are made
we accept that we could lose the money we paid to go to auction but that a risk we prepared to take say julie widlake
the secret of a successful outcome depends partly on setting the right reserve price a task the auctioneer undertakes in conjunction with the seller
normally the reserve is set only day or hour before the auction when the agent will already have a good indication of how much interest ha been shown
too high a reserve price can mean no sale and disappointment all round
you need to understand what your client expectation are beforehand say graham harrison of bristol and west
agent and their client may also have the dilemma of deciding whether to accept any offer made prior to the auction
inevitably they do not always get it right
peter crowther managing director of a leeds business centre recently bought two stone cottage in bramhope on the outskirt of leeds at an auction in the village pub
his successful bid wa for although he had made a higher prior offer which had been turned down
on the other hand sometimes the drama of the auction and the competition between bidder can have the opposite effect
another recent auction in leeds saw a stone farmhouse without water or other amenity finally fall under the hammer for
success is by no mean guaranteed at auction say graham harrison
in a tough market you need to get the programme right the price right and have a little bit of luck

a prayer for the brick cathedral facing st paul bankside power station is a masterpiece worth preserving gavin stamp argues
by gavin stamp
from the top of the dome of st paul cathedral the view is no longer dominated by city church steeple but by an intrusive cacophony of drab characterless sixty box
one building stand out in this dispiriting panorama of mediocrity a dark powerful mass of brickwork with a tall central tower that stand right across the thames from wren dome
this is not an office block nor a church although it sublime form might suggest that it architect wa adept at designing cathedral
it is in fact the now redundant electric power station that sits on bankside next to the site of sam wanamaker new globe theatre
bankside power station should never have been built
it architect had spent the war year with fellow royal academician planning the orderly and spacious london of the future free of smoke and industry
but when asked in to replace an old dirty power station that had been on the site since he soon forgot such idealism and like any architect wa glad to have the job
the project wa controversial and the power station wa only permitted providing the smoke wa clean and the building did not challenge the visual dominance of st paul
so the single chimney rose only to some below the height of the cross above the cathedral
the irony is that had the tower been higher and had the teak scrubber been le efficient the smoke would have gone straight up into the air
a it wa the smokeless shimmer of vapour wa so cooled by cleaning that it drifted across the river to cause mischief with the leadwork on wren great dome
bankside power station should not have been built
but a it wa built it should not now be demolished
that is because it is a magnificent structure the supreme architectural expression of the heroic monumental phase of power station design and the creation of a great architect
bankside wa the work of sir giles gilbert scott om the architect of liverpool anglican cathedral the rebuilt house of common and some of the last vital product of the gothic revival
he wa a designer of extraordinary versatility being responsible for the standard traditional red telephone kiosk waterloo bridge and several power station
bankside represents the fullest realisation of his industrial aesthetic
scott first venture into this unlikely field of design wa at battersea where in he wa wheeled in a a famous knighted architect by the london power company to try to make acceptable the monster power station to which the resident of chelsea and westminster were taking strong exception
this wa a brilliant move
scott wa so successful in styling the building in fine brickwork with fluting a john betjeman called it that when the battersea a station wa opened in it wa widely acclaimed a a supremely successful modern treatment of a building type that seemed quintessentially twentieth century
when in the architect journal conducted a survey to find what were considered the best modern building in britain battersea wa placed second and wa the favourite of such unlikely celebrity a sir kenneth clark rebecca west and charles laughton
scott wa so pleased with the style he had evolved at battersea a treatment that humanised industrial form without denying their function that he also used it on the guinness factory at park royal west london
at battersea scott could not alter the basic design of the building and he much disliked the upturned table appearance created by the four corner chimney
at bankside however he wa able to persuade the engineer mott hay anderson to gather all the flue into a single slender tower or campanile
a a result he wa able to create a symmetrical monumental composition of great power
a at all his power station scott faced the building in a fine worcestershire brick that ha weathered to a lovely
but there is nothing homely about the general effect
vast overlapping plane of brickwork are modelled with careful and subtle band of detail
the result is an expression of the monumental aesthetic of the early twentieth century with strong american overtone
when the campanile is seen from a distance it seems to belong to some strange expressionist church one ha not noticed before
not for nothing were such power station described a brick cathedral bankside is the finest manifestation of this tradition
now it is redundant
smoke shimmer no longer from the tall tower
but bankside is nevertheless a sound structure which like the best mill of the industrial revolution is well worth preserving and is perfectly capable of adaptation for a new commercial use
such is of course much encouraged by a building being listed something which until recently wa not possible with architecture of so recent a date
two year ago however the department of the environment at last began the listing of building in england that were more than year old
bracken house the former home of the financial time became the first candidate and english heritage then submitted some recommendation to the department of the environment these included bankside
this however wa too much for the government and using the excuse that public opinion wa not yet ready to accept the protection of many unpopular modern building lord caithness the minister of state for the environment arbitrarily whittled down english heritage list to building excluding bankside although it represented a more traditional approach in the fifty to the modern movement
however caithness himself stated that this first selection wa in no way a definitive list
i have no doubt that others will be added
the important thing is that the thirty year rule is in force and that we can respond to developing perception of our time
earlier this year in my capacity a chairman of the thirty society i asked caithness successor virginia bottomley to reconsider english heritage recommendation of bankside for listing
my argument wa that a michael heseltine had so boldly listed battersea power station in it wa illogical not to protect a much finer and more complete industrial work by the same architect
furthermore the listing of battersea had ensured the building survival for conversion to a new use in that case a an entertainment centre which the prime minister herself had praised and inaugurated
after two month silence i wa informed that minister stood by their decision
i wrote back asking the reason for this pointing out that if any large modern power station deserved to be listed it wa bankside
i have received no satisfactory reply
of course i know perfectly well why the department of the environment decline to list it
listed building procedure might impede the full commercial realisation of the site when the electricity industry is privatised
furthermore british rail ha it eye on the bankside site for bringing up the spoil from the tunnel for channel traffic which it is so absurdly driving under the middle of london at astronomical cost
listing in theory is an objective assessment of architectural or historical importance which doe not necessarily prevent demolition
in the case of bankside power station the ultimate temple of power and a masterpiece of industrial architecture by a major british architect our historic building system is being perverted for purely political reason
her dress hang here the kahlo cult
oriana baddeley
the have witnessed a shift in the art establishment attitude towards art produced outside of it traditional parameter
the work of previously marginalised artist ha become an area of rich speculation among art dealer priced out of the modern master market
almost every year ha witnessed the discovery of new artistic terrain graffiti art soviet art australian art the art of latin america
the major auction house have moved with the time and have found new way of selling work which in both form and content would have proved an unstable investment a decade ago
the current status of the work of the mexican painter frida kahlo is a dramatic example of this change
once known primarily a the wife of diego rivera her reputation outside of mexico now far supercedes his since sale room estimate of her work have risen from to over million and in a work by kahlo broke all record at sotheby new york for a latin american artist
the enormous rise in the economic value of her work ha developed in tandem with the increased critical and popular response to her particular blend of naive style and incisive content
while the first wave of popular interest arose with the whitechapel exhibition instigated by laura mulvey and peter wollen it wa the publication of hayden herrera biography of kahlo in which ha led to her current cult status
since that date she ha been the subject of tv documentary a feature film frida by paul leduc a stage play numerous publication and the inspiration for designer clothing

a with most artist who have become mythical personality in the popular imagination such attention ha focused primarily on the anecdotal and tragic detail of kahlo admittedly fascinating life
the passionate obsession with her husband diego rivera her flamboyant appearance but most of all her physical and emotional pain have come to dominate response to her work
while kahlo art helped her to deal with the vicissitude of her life for most audience it is her life story which allows access to her art
in this one can draw obvious parallel to the appeal of van gogh a traditionally popular artist recently made fashionable by the medium attention generated during the centennial of his death
the archetypal became an appropriate icon for the sixty revival of long hot summer
yet despite the iconic status of van gogh tragic life it is the appearance of his work by which he is ultimately signified his thick impasto his vibrant yellow the urgency of his creative drive
in the case of kahlo the popular image is of the artist herself the characteristic brow the elaborate hair the mexican costume fig
it is primarily her appearance not the formal language of her art that ha graced the page of elle and vogue magazine

in the later vogue piece only the style remained a the far more overtly sexual kahloesque model lounged and pouted in their mexican interior

of course the line between art and life is a particularly hard one to draw in kahlo case
the majority of her work is self portraiture her aesthetic concern grew from her fascination with the falsity of appearance
dressing up role playing and masquerade form the conceptual basis of kahlo work
in with cropped hair fig she paint herself wearing rivera suit challenging traditional expectation of femininity and attempting to appropriate his authority while simultaneously threatening castration

the impossibility stemmed from the failure of such follower to recognise the symbolic importance of kahlo choice of clothing a failure also intrinsic to her recent magazine appearance
the particularity of mexico are frequently subsumed by the decorativeness of the ethnic by the generalised attractiveness of the radical
for kahlo however choosing to don the costume of the tehuana a for example in tree of hope fig wa to embody a powerful icon of cultural identity
mexican indian dress is extraordinarily diverse and by and large geographically specific varying from region to region
the tehuana dress is by no mean the most decorative variant or the closest to form of clothing
it is the mythology surrounding the woman wearer of the costume which directed kahlo choice
the ostensibly matriarchal society of tehuantepec led to the adoption of the tehuana in mexico a the image of the strong indian woman the undefeated counterpart to the despised chingada who conversely is the female embodiment of mexico hybrid culture
in a culture where sexual metaphor are frequently used to convey racial and political conflict the tehuana represents that aspect of mexico indigenous tradition unbowed by century of colonial and male rule
kahlo adoption of tehuana dress while being an attractive disguise of what she saw a a le than perfect body asserted both a feminist and an position

in this painting a memorial to a woman tragic death is transformed into an indictment of the culture which destroyed her

the story behind hale death wa one with which kahlo obviously identified and within which dress formed an important symbolic function

in kahlo painting the figure fall from the fantasy world she ha inhabited to the harsh bloodspattered reality of the street literally coming down to earth

the painting dedicated to hale mother wa commissioned by a mutual friend of kahlo and dorothy hale the managing editor of vanity fair clare boothe luce

hale black velvet dress is cursed because it represents the value of the gringolandia so hated by kahlo
in those painting where kahlo wear european dress she is passive weak and unable to control her own destiny but in the tehuana costume she is strong powerful hopeful
unclothed her body becomes yet more vulnerable but a jean franco state
the unclothed body is not a self but a socialised body a body that is opened by instrument technologized wounded it organ displayed to the outside world
the inner frida is controlled by modern society far more than the clothed frida who often mark her deviation from the norm by defiantly returning the gaze of the viewer
kahlo naked body becomes not just the tortured self of her personal biography but a visual counterpart to the injured and defiled manifestation of mexico colonised past la llorona the weeping woman of popular myth and la chingada the raped and abused mother described in paz the labyrinth of solitude
descended from an aztec mother goddess llorona is a mother figure symbolic in a wider sense of the trauma of the spanish invasion
driven mad with grief by the loss of her child she is thought to wander the street weeping and cry out a ghostly memory of the past
at it most simple la chingada a the mother of mestizo culture is the mother forcibly opened violated or deceived
the female soil possessed and misused by the masculine force of the spanish invader
the indian mexico raped and abused by the conquistador yet bearing his bastard child
the rhetoric of the tehuana opposes the nihilism of traditional feminisation of colonial trauma and asserts the potential of a dignified cultural resistance

law report
parliament urged to think again on housing issue
queen bench divisional court sandwell metropolitan borough council v bujok before lord justice watkins and mr justice hutchison november
if a dwelling house is in such a state of disrepair a to be prejudicial to health or a nuisance the tenant may lay an information against his landlord alleging the existence of a statutory nuisance under the public health act
the tenant is not obliged to ensure that the landlord is aware of the defect in the premise or to give the landlord an opportunity to remedy the defect before commencing legal proceeding
although that is the position in law the court emphasised that a a matter of commonsense a tenant should first complain to the landlord before exercising the right to prosecute
the fact
mr bujok and her family occupied a house a council tenant
in september mr bujok laid an information against the council alleging the existence and continuance of a statutory nuisance under section of the public health act
it wa alleged that the council being the owner of the premise were the person by whose act default or sufferance the nuisance arose
prior to laying the information mr bujok had not served an abatement notice upon the council or informed them of the alleged defect in the premise
the justice held mr bujok wa not required to ensure that the council were aware of the defective state of the property prior to laying the information
the council appealed by case stated
the legislation
section of the act defines statutory nuisance a any premise in such a state a to be prejudicial to health or a nuisance
the decision
mr justice hutchison said the act primarily envisages a system where the local authority ha a power and a duty to try to secure that premise are not in a state which constitutes a statutory nuisance
action is initiated by the service of an abatement notice requiring remedial work
if the person in default fails to comply with an abatement notice the local authority is obliged to make a complaint to the magistrate
if the complaint is proved a nuisance order is made requiring the defendant to get the necessary work done
effectively the sequence is that the person in default is told what is wrong and is required to put it right
he is given an opportunity to do so and if he doe not he is subject to sanction by the court to compel him to do so
the problem arises in connection with section which adapts or applies the provision to case where an individual rather than the local authority wish to make the complaint
need he serve an abatement notice
the authority plainly establish that he need not and can not do so
doe that mean he may lay an information and bring the matter before the magistrate without first putting the person alleged to be in default on notice of what is alleged
the council argued that a landlord particularly one such a a local authority can not realistically be expected to have a system of inspection of all it premise and in practice is entitled to depend upon notification by it tenant
for mr bujok it wa argued that the act wa designed to secure in the interest of the community at large that statutory nuisance did not exist
it wa submitted that an owner can not turn his back on his property because when he purchase and take on the responsibility of letting he know the property will in the course of time deteriorate
he must therefore satisfy himself on a regular basis that it doe not constitute a statutory nuisance
in warner v lambeth london borough council hlr lord justice glidewell said a private person could lay an information alleging the failure to abate a statutory nuisance without first giving notice requiring abatement
therefore in the present case the justice came to the correct conclusion
his lordship reached that decision without enthusiasm because it seemed that a a matter of common sense notice should be given in such circumstance before criminal proceeding were launched
lord justice watkins said he agreed with reluctance
it wa surely repugnant to commonsense that in this area of legal activity a local authority should be prosecuted by one of it tenant without first being given the opportunity by that tenant to remedy the consequence of a neglect to repair the dwelling that the tenant occupied
in law there wa no doubt that mr bujok wa entitled to commence proceeding without giving notice of the state of the dwelling to the council
but in every other conceivable way that action wa entirely wrong
endless trouble to many people in court and council office and much money could be saved by the giving of notice of disrepair
if the council did not react to that notice then would be the time for the tenant to exercise the right to prosecute
parliament should give fresh thought to enacting a provision placing an obligation upon a council tenant to give notice to the council before being permitted to commence proceeding
appearance john cherryman qc instructed by sherwood co for the council elizabeth norman instructed by michael arnold co oldbury for mr bujok
shiranikha herbert barrister

prototyping is crucial to system development argues ian richards tailored to fit
in system development nothing is more fundamental than assessing user requirement
if you do know what the system is required to do you do know anything
but many system developer are unable to ass requirement properly
they seem to think that you can ask a businessman what his requirement are and get an answer that amount to a draft system specification
a doctor doe ask his patient what treatment to prescribe
the patient can explain only what the problem is
it is the doctor that provides the remedy
if you ask a user what sort of system he want you will be met with a blank look
a user may have a deep knowledge of business problem but knowing little about computer ha no idea how they should be tackled
yet analyst are heard asking time and again tell me what you want
we gone awayfrom the day of system imposed by the data processing department this is going to be a system for the user
but of course the user do know what they want so they end up getting another duff system
an effective analyst provides the same service to the business a the doctor provides to the patient
he find out what the need of the business are and prescribes the cure
the user tell the analyst what the problem are and the analyst decides at least in broad term what the user requires
but the analyst ha one great advantage over the doctor
once the user becomes familiar with the proposed system helpful comment come thick and fast
oh this will be of great help in ordering raw material but sometimes we get part delivery could we have an extra facility to deal with those
and sometimes discount is given a pig to deal with on the old system but if you could add one extra input box on that screen there
and what about order not delivered on time
if we could list those we have advance warning of shortage problem on the assembly line two month before they occur
now that would be a great leap forward
unfortunately you can not reach this stage until you have developed a prototype system
and you ca develop a prototype system because the user have got a clue what they want
most of them are probably muttering i too busy to get involved in this sort of thing
what wrong with the old system anyway
the only way to develop a prototype is for the analyst to get inside the head of the user and thinking like a user decide what sort of system is required
of course the initial system will not be perfect
the analyst can not hope to understand the business a well in a few week a the user doe after many year
but once the user see the system channel of communication will open
instead of persuading the user to specify requirement the analyst will be driven by the user to meet key need
good system development go through two distinct phase
initially the analyst doe all the work leading the user towards a system he think is right for the business
but once the user see the potential of the system a change in attitude take place
the process becomes demand driven by the user
the analyst is then forced on the defensive explaining why new feature can not be included because they are technically difficult or prohibitively expensive
traditionally system were validated by user agreeing functional specification
in theory validation meant that the user had read the specification imagined how the system would work in practice and agreed the design
it wa only when using a test version of the system available just before the planned implementation date that difficulty would come to light and a host of change request be issued
the advent of fourth generation language ha made system development much easier
with a an initial prototype can be put together quickly
this mean feedback is obtained early in the development process and the system can grow around the user requirement
crucial to the development process is the relationship built up between the analyst and the user
the best system arise when both have a deep understanding of each other job
many developer use business analyst to ensure that the development team maintain a proper focus on business requirement
but this can be a it cut off communication between the system analyst and the user
too much specialisation is bad for system development it feed the temptation to get engrossed in technical difficulty and forget about the underlying business need
if you should stroll into a pub and meet an analyst and a user talking about work and you can not tell one from the other they have probably developed a successful system together
ian richards book how to use a computer to improve your business ha just been published by graham trotman paperback hardback

edoardo amaldi
ragazzi of distinction
in december the men working feverishly to create the first american atomic bomb sent a team of spook to naples
one of their main assignment wa to contact edoardo amaldi a physicist thought to be in hiding near rome
six month later the day before rome liberation by the ally amaldi wa found

midwife at the birth of a state
the intifada is a people unarmed revolution against occupation
it two main slogan repeated countless time in the directive issued by the underground leadership are freedom and independence
it ha employed a dual strategy to achieve these two objective
first a comprehensive civil disobedience campaign wa begun by which people severed or minimised all the contact point by which they were bound to the israeli occupation authority
this campaign included resignation of palestinian official from public post the boycott of israeli good and product and the refusal to pay tax and fine
partial and full strike demonstration convention all these have in fact only constituted the outer layer of an inner mechanism of civilian rebellion
the second and complementary part of the intifada strategy concentrated on the construction of an indigenous national authority
a israel authority wa being lifted the population began creating an alternative authority of their own
popular committee were established in village refugee camp suburb street in fact in every community
some headway wa made in expanding whether through utilising more land for agriculture developing home economy or encouraging local manufacturer and product
village and refugee camp were thus being developed into liberated or independent area if not militarily then at least psychologically politically and infrastructurally
bloody clash would occur whenever armoured unit raided these village storming through makeshift defensive road block and responding to rock being thrown with live bullet and tear gas but no sooner would these army unit be gone than authority would revert to the village resident
palestinian flag would be raised on minaret and church spire road block would again be erected and life in all it aspect would once again be run by the local leadership
the structure of the developing national authority ha been both diffuse enough to prevent it from being destroyed by any one single sweep of arrest there have been more than arrest since the intifada outbreak and coherent enough to allow for the existence of a unified resistance strategy
while the entire network of popular committee local institution and the general public constitute the field commander in the battle of civilian disobedience and of constructing a political infrastructure a rotating unified national command act in the role of issuing a directive outlining policy and determining specific resistance programme
a high level of mobility in the structure allows for continuous interchange of role and idea and retains for the unified national command the closeness to grass root that is required to make it truly reflect people wish and sentiment
this expanded network of popular committee and institution making up the unified leadership is infused by ten of thousand of activist who belong to or identify with the different faction of the plo
in effect therefore the plo exists at all level of organisation within the occupied territory
thus the palestinian national movement both inside and outside the occupied territory is an organic whole
the pattern of the intifada ha been cyclical
thrust of resistance mass demonstration resignation tax rebellion etc would come in crest
the pattern is determined by a wide variety of factor including what the israeli army doe
but the relation is complex not
harsh measure putting an entire community under an absolute curfew for a continuous lengthy period of time demolishing home uprooting olive or citrus tree physical intimidation and terror tactic employed by raiding army unit shooting killing cutting off water or electricity supply and telephone link to village or town mass arrest intimidatory interrogation technique can either create a temporary lull or activate an eruption
the army never know which it will be
it is a if it is walking through a minefield
the pattern of the intifada it pain and suffering are all reminiscent of the process of birth
the metaphor is apt a palestinian regard themselves a engaging in a process of giving birth to their independent palestinian state
through their revolution the mass are both mother and midwife to the birth of this state
the intifada is the midwife of freedom
through it palestinian are struggling on a daily basis to shake off israel authority and to construct their own
the struggle reflects a revolution in mass consciousness by which people have come to realise that idea and aspiration must be embodied in manifest act if reality is to be changed
thus wherever one look one find people engaged in the construction of the block that will make up the palestinian state
it is a conscious effort
the mass are being engaged in the craft of
in this process of state building many stage have been covered
the declaration of independence issued by the palestine national council pnc on november last year constitutes a major landmark along this road
it significance lie in it double message that the aim of the palestinian struggle is the establishment of palestinian independence and that this independence is regarded a being not at israel expense
this ha been a constant theme of intifada policy that we wish to build palestine not to destroy israel that we wish to achieve freedom for our people not to deprive others israeli of it that we wish to protect and save life ours not to endanger the life of others israeli
in one of several intifada leaflet written in hebrew and addressed to the israeli soldier on duty in the occupied territory the message wa repeated soldier go home
return to your family and child
be with them in peace so that we may remain with our family and child in peace
we do not wish to harm you or your state
we wish to be unharmed in our own state
how can the process of state building be developed
if the pnc declaration of independence constituted a major landmark in this process the time ha come to embark on another major step that of declaring the setting up of a state or government structure
an escalation of the intifada in this direction would serve two purpose at once
first it would consolidate the structure of the developing national authority which is competing to replace the occupation authority
second it would consolidate the image and essence of the intifada a a constructive not a destructive force
naturally to embark on such a step is not necessarily to succeed immediately in realising it
rather it is a challenge
it will be a further challenge to israel occupation conceived in the image of earlier challenge of the intifada
but it will also be a challenge to u palestinian summoning u to work more energetically towards the idea fulfilment
it would be a natural extension of the intifada dual strategy towards disengagement from israel and the corresponding process of state building
it would further naturalise and legitimise the evolving skeletal form of palestinian independence
it would provide the multitudinous popular committee and activity with a more advanced form of organisation and structure
it would enable better planning and performance
it would maximise civilian tactic of resistance and defuse the natural potential for violence containing and eventually eliminating the marginal but intrusive phenomenon of collaborator activation by israeli security authority and collaborator execution by local palestinian
it would create a further fact that would put israel on the spot
israel reaction however hostile could only further our cause
arresting or deporting the ten of thousand of palestinian professional who would be employed in perfectly apolitical harmless and humanitarian job can only further isolate the israeli government
measure can only imply success
a modus vivendi would also imply success
in general our policy should be to proceed with building our state block by block without waiting to be given a gift of it through negotiation
we should regard negotiation rather a the mean by which we could establish formal agreement between our state and israel
such agreement can range from the issue of border to the issue of free for our future television and radio network
in the meantime we have the capacity to bring coherence and organisation to a whole range of activity further consolidating the institutional linkage between the people in the occupied state and the plo leadership
entire department can be set up in health foreign affair agriculture trade finance education justice religion information and social welfare
a pyramid administrative structure establishing link from popular committee in village right up to the executive committee of the plo in it capacity a a cabinet can be established
during the intifada the people have been engaged in building the side wall
a government would provide the roof which would bring these wall together
it would add another necessary touch in the process of creating a palestinian home
