the government initiative have to some extent reflected a diagnosis based on the need for better management though on the principle that central authority can provide a firmer grip than local one but combined with an belief in the restorative power of capitalism
leech and amin summarize this approach not unfairly in the following term
the encouragement of private investment and the liberation of the market the containment of the force of social discontent the control of the power of the local authority and the encouragement of the movement of the wealthy into the inner city thus creating buffer area of tory support accentuating inequality and injustice and hopefully though not necessarily reducing the potential for conflict among the urban poor
the main thrust of the government policy is contained in the january white paper on regional policy and the enterprise economy in the new employment training programme and especially in the march action for city programme all resting on wider reform to local government structure and finance and to education and housing
the most striking feature of this package apart from it aim actively to involve employer and entrepreneur is a sharp reduction in the role of local government
despite the contemporary tone of much of action for city the programme heritage can be traced to the early study which provided the basis for the holland report on housing and the plowden report on education a a result of which general improvement area and education priority area were established
the urban programme had a social rather than economic emphasis and wa administered by the home office
it wa initiated partly in response to the furore caused by enoch powell river of blood speech much a disturbance at the notting hill carnival prompted further step on the part of the department of the environment a riot make a much bigger impact on government thinking a donnison ha pointed out than any amount of earnest and accurate research
the urban programme consisted of grant and initiative under the local government grant social need act which wa intended a a flexible instrument to provide supplementary help to local authority in the field of housing education and health
originally the programme supplemented existing central and local government scheme designed to meet special need in urban area
the scope wa extended in an enhanced urban programme which included economic and environmental a well a social project and wa specifically directed at the inner urban area where the problem were most severe
earlier the change of emphasis from a social to an economic and environmental focus had been reflected in a switch of responsibility for the programme from the home office to the department of the environment
the enhanced programme resulted from the inner urban area act based on a white paper published the previous year on policy for the inner city doe the first comprehensive policy statement on the subject to acknowledge it a a definable and cohesive problem
the white paper drew on study conducted earlier in the decade in liverpool birmingham and london which pointed to a debilitating flight of capital and skilled labour from the critical area of deprivation
a key aspect of the white paper wa the stress it placed on the wider effect of poverty that it wa not just those with acute need who suffered
it argued that in talking about inner city it wa vital to think in term not just of individual but of society that the multiple deprivation of the worst hit area affected all the resident that the consequence included a pervasive sense of neglect and decay a decline in community spirit a low standard of neighbourhood facility and an increase in crime and vandalism and that without government intervention the future wa one of reduced job opportunity deteriorating housing and a decline in public service
the document and the legislation that derived from it pointed to a positively discriminatory approach with both central and local government supplementing existing programme in such a way a to strengthen local economy a well a the physical and social environment
such measure constituted the present government heritage when it took office in
none of them of course anticipated the scale of the problem which were caused by the slump and collapse of much of what remained of inner urban manufacturing industry in the early
neither at first did the incoming administration foresee the impact of rising unemployment which wa to be especially serious among the urban young
true the new secretary of state for the environment laid stress from the outset on the need for economic regeneration and indicated his sympathy for the voluntary sector in the tackling of urban problem
the previous government however had already pointed to the need to revitalize urban economy and at first the shift wa more rhetorical than real
michael heseltine ha since claimed that we set a new objective to make the inner city place where people would want to live and work and where the private investor would be willing to put his money
partnership became his slogan the partnership of public and private brain and money
a new urban development grant wa devised to with public fund scheme which would then attract private investment
heseltine vision wa of partnership which recognise that there are some thing that only government can pay for but also that the ingenuity and flexibility of the private sector is indispensable
he claim that serious work on policy began in but it wa undoubtedly the riot of coinciding with the biggest drop in employment and job vacancy since the war which gave impetus to the new approach
urban development corporation were introduced in in london docklands and merseyside and the urban development grant came in late the following year
conservative instinct were of course to minimize within the partnership state involvement and expenditure relative to that of private enterprise
yet the irony of the early a a deteriorating but perennial urban problem rapidly became the most acute aspect of the crisis of mass unemployment wa that a tory government found itself presiding over an increase in state intervention through a variety of agency
the increased scale of operation also ushered in another fashion of the new management structure
thus in city action team were introduced to each inner city partnership area to the work of the three government department involved
task force meanwhile were directed to tackle youth unemployment
by the urban programme wa supporting starter unit and business start in enterprise workshop
it wa providing training place often in conjunction with the manpower service commission some building were being improved estate action aimed to tackle run down housing and a large number of new partnership which some might see a subsidy or discredited regional grant in a new guise were in operation in an effort to bring private investment to urban area
by it wa claimed that million of urban development grant and urban regeneration grant had successfully levered more than million of private investment into the inner city although how much of the latter sum might have been invested in any case is difficult to say
meanwhile there were other incentive scheme enterprise zone for example and simplified planning zone which aimed to lift tax and planning barrier in order to facilitate investment
indeed while with one hand trying to hold down expenditure by local authority the government found itself by the late involved with the other hand in massive spending on inner urban area
the department of the environment alone by wa spending half a billion pound out of an action for city total involving most home department estimated at billion
perhaps a labour government would have spent even more it would certainly have spent it in different way
it is a curious comment on thatcherism however that the administration most committed to a reduction in the role of the state and in the need for an independent private sector ha spent more on specific urban regeneration and employment scheme and incentive to private investment in urban area than any other in recent history
one of the most bizarre aspect of government policy ha been the effective murder of the voluntary sector and it appropriation by subterfuge into the tory version of the corporate state
conservative have always lauded the voluntarist principle in welfare and encouraged it from platform
faced however with the catastrophic increase in unemployment and the need to occupy large number of workless people without directly employing them which would have run counter to the economic doctrine which had led to the redundancy of many of them in the first place the government poured money into any voluntary agency willing to put in a bid for cheap labour
one result wa the triumphant expansion of some charitable organization which rejoiced both at their importance and at the government munificence
another wa the transformation of many such body already heavily subsidized from public fund into de facto agency of the state which financed them and indirectly determined their policy
nowhere wa the impact of this clumsy sleight of hand more evident than in the inner city where voluntary organization had been most active and where the government wa most anxious for them to mop up unemployment
however the later withdrawal of government support with the scrapping of the community programme a unemployment receded left many of these voluntary organization high and dry
the national council for voluntary organization ncvo ha suggested from a recent survey that around project had been affected and had lost million in funding macgregor
there wa of course a crucial element in the government anxiety the high concentration of ethnic minority in the area of concern
in nearly per cent of ethnic minority in the uk lived in partnership or programme area
there is a danger in reading back from this figure another stereotype similar to the pavlovian drug city assumed link
some urban area have serious problem without a major ethnic dimension newcastle teesside not all member of ethnic minority are poor or deprived
nevertheless the high proportion of inner urban population composed of people from ethnic minority and the high incidence among these group of all the index of poverty and social and environmental hardship combined with the specific problem of rivalry harassment and tension make race and ethnicity an aspect that is central to any analysis of the inner city and of any ameliorative approach
making sense of the riot
reaction to the riot have concentrated on a number of key variable that are said to characterize the locality in which the riot have occurred
lord scarman report on the disorder highlighted the importance of unemployment urban deprivation racial disadvantage relation between young black and the police the decline of civic consent and political exclusion a the key issue
other reaction have concentrated on the issue of the interplay between decay and racial disadvantage in contemporary britain
yet others have argued that the unrest can be seen a a symptom of the breakdown of law and order in british society gaffney hall keith
the main issue that were prominent in debate during were race and law and order
this wa by no mean an accident since throughout the a powerful body of medium political and academic opinion had been constructed around the theme of how britain wa drifting into a violent society and how the basis of consent wa being shifted by the pressure of immigration and the growth of inner city area
a glimpse of the impact of the riot at this level can be achieved through two important debate in parliament
the first took place in the midst of the july riot and had a it theme civil disturbance
the tone of the debate wa set by home secretary william whitelaw introductory statement in which he spoke of a the need to remove the scourge of criminal violence from our street and b the urgency of developing policy designed to promote the mutual tolerance and understanding upon which the whole future of a free democratic society depends hansard vol july
the scourge of criminal violence wa whitelaw argued a danger to the whole framework of consent and legality on which the political institution of british society were based
in reply roy hattersley supported the call for the immediate suppression of street violence but warned that the root of such riot could not be dealt with until all people felt they had a stake in british society ibid col
the second debate took place on november on the publication of the scarman report and had a it theme law and order
the importance of the riot in pushing the law and order issue and specifically policing on to the main political agenda wa emphasized by the liberal leader david steel who argued that urgent action to prevent a drift into lawlessness wa necessary from both a moral and a political perspective hansard vol november col
a subsequent debate on the same issue in march wa also full of reference to the experience of the impact of street violence crime decaying urban condition the breakdown of consent between the police and many local community and the spectre of more violence to come if change in both policing tactic and social policy were not swiftly introduced hansard vol march col
the need to support the police wa accepted by both the labour and the conservative speaker in the parliamentary debate on the riot and wa established a a benchmark for the official response to the riot long before the scarman report wa published in november
any substantive disagreement centred around the issue of what role social deprivation and unemployment had in bringing young people to protest violently on the street
intermingled with the discourse about race and law and order were constant reference to unemployment particularly among the young and various form of social disadvantage and poverty solomos pp
throughout and debate about the riot in the medium in parliament and in various official report hinged around the interrelationship between racial and social factor
the importance of this debate can be explained partly by the political capital which the opposition could make from linking the social and economic malaise of the country at large with violent street disturbance
conversely throughout this period government minister strenuously denied that unemployment and social deprivation were significant cause of urban unrest
although the scarman report is often taken to be the central text which argues for a link between social condition and disorder the term of the debate were by no mean set by scarman
during both april and july vigorous exchange took place in the press and in parliament about the role that deteriorating social condition and unemployment may have played in bringing about the riot
during the july parliamentary debate on civil disturbance roy hattersley formulation of this linkage provided a useful summary of the social condition argument
after some preliminary remark about the labour party support for the police he went on to outline his opposition to the view of the riot a essentially outburst
i repeat that l do not believe that the principal cause of last week riot wa the conduct of the police
it wa the condition of deprivation and despair in the decaying area of our old city area in which the brixton and toxteth riot took place and area from which the skinhead invader of southall come
hansard vol july
much of the subsequent controversy about this analysis centred on the question of youth unemployment
hattersley had suggested that the riot were a direct product of high level of youth unemployment and a furious debate ensued in both parliament and the medium about this assertion
the final symbolic cue used to make sense of the protest is more difficult to categorize but it basic meaning can be captured by the term political marginality
while a number of discussion of the root of urban unrest in the united state have noted the salience of political marginality in determining participation in violent protest skolnick fogelson edelman knopf this issue ha received relatively little attention in britain
nevertheless during the event and their aftermath the political context wa discussed from a number of perspective
the scarman report for example located part of the explanation for the riot in the feeling of alienation and powerlessness which were experienced by young black living in depressed area
a successful policy for tackling the root of urban disorder wa seen a one which sought to involve all the community in dealing with the problem of each area so that they could come to feel that they have a stake in it future scarman para
where such argument did not fit in with the overarching theme of race violence and disorder and social deprivation they were either sidelined or pushed into the of official report
the scarman report for example contained the following policy proposal i recommend that local community must be fully and effectively involved in planning in the provision of local service and in the management and financing of specific project scarman para
such a move towards greater political integration wa seen by lord scarman a essential if the gap between resident and the force of law and order wa to be bridged
but the concern with overcoming political marginality remained on the sideline of the main public debate because it questioned the perception of the rioter a driven by irrational uncivilized and criminal instinct
this did not however stop the question of political marginality and the need to reform existing policy from being raised at all a can be seen subsequently by the attempt after to introduce both locally and nationally measure which were meant to address some of the grievance of the rioter and to ensure that further disturbance did not occur
aspect of these measure are considered further on in the chapter
perspective on the riot
despite widespread prediction of further unrest in the aftermath of the scale and the location of the riot seem to have surprised even some of the most astute commentator
handsworth for example wa presented even shortly before september a a success story in term of police community relation
the outbreak of violence in this area wa therefore widely presented a an aberration
similarly the spread of violence in london to area such a the broadwater farm estate in tottenham wa seen a a break from previous experience which had centred on area such a brixton
there are many continuity between and in relation to the image used in the press and television to cover the event
but response in were different at least in term of degree and probably in relation to the extent to which the riot were seen a a race phenomenon by a wider body of opinion
the ambiguity and to be found in much of the press coverage during had at least acted a a countervailing tendency against the more extreme form of discourse which blamed the riot completely on black people
during the riot and their immediate aftermath the imagery of race wa used by section of the press without the sense of ambiguity which could still be found in
the silence over race wa breached in but in debate about racial issue wa taken a step further
peregrine worsthorne for example used the ferocity of the confrontation in handsworth brixton and tottenham to argue that there wa a major question mark over the possibility of assimilating the coloured population into mainstream british value sunday telegraph september
to be sure there wa still a strong response opposing enoch powell call for repatriation from all shade of political opinion but the racialization of public debate about the riot went much further than
in this context it wa the externality of british and asian which wa highlighted rather the racist institution and process which worked against black at all level of society
the usage of race during the period took on new meaning which had little if anything to do with the impact of racism a such since the emphasis wa on the cultural characteristic of the minority community themselves
after handsworth part of the press response wa to blame the riot on rivalry between west indian and asian and even after the argument were criticized by local resident and community leader they were used to explain what happened
in addition the question whether the culture and value of the black community their family structure and their political attitude bred violence wa constantly raised van dijk
the actual fact of who wa arrested during the riot whether black or white were hardly debated since it wa assumed that they were mostly black and mostly unemployed and involved with crime keith
the imagery of the black bomber used in handsworth wa extended to the notion that there were group of alienated and criminalized young black who saw the riot a a chance to engage in an orgy of looting
the dear report on handsworth capture this image and link it to the social condition of young black
the majority of rioter who took part in these unhappy event were young black and origin
let there be no doubt these young criminal are not in any way representative of the vast majority of the community whose life ha contributed to the life and culture of the west midland over many year and whose hope and aspiration are at one with those of every other citizen
we share a common sorrow
it is the duty of u all to ensure that an entire cultural group is not tainted by the action of a criminal minority
dear
this black criminal minority wa constructed not only into the leading force behind the riot but sometimes a the only force
indeed throughout september and october and during the following month the imagery of race continued to dominate debate about both the cause and the policy outcome of the riot
a pointed out earlier the social cause argument wa another major plank of public debate about the riot particularly in relation to the highly politicized issue of unemployment
during this issue wa raised once again though by then the extent of mass unemployment and urban and decay wa more stark than it had been in
image of urban decay tinderbox city and ghetto street linked up with the image of race inequality and black ghetto to produce an analysis more complex but also more contradictory
an interesting mixture of the various image wa provided by a story in the daily telegraph under the headline broadwater farm like the divis flat with reggae october
the mirror described the estate a living hell and quoted one resident a saying that you no idea how awful daily life is october
such image were reworkings of argument already used about toxteth in and brixton in but they were used more widely than in
even the daily mail which deployed the clearest use of race and outside agitator argument ran a major story on broadwater farm under the headline hulk litter this concrete jungle despair hang heavy october
a number of story using such imagery were run by both the quality and the popular press during this period but similar argument are to be found in parliamentary debate hansard vol october col and even in official report produced by the police on the riot in birmingham and london
the city of inner despair were conceived a the breeding ground for disorderly protest and however hard the government tried to break the causal link between the two it wa forced to take on board the need to restore order not only through the police but through promise of help for the inner city
much a in the social cause argument can not be seen separately from the broader debate about the future of the british economy and society
the government record on unemployment wa a heavily politicized issue and just a in it vehemently denied any responsibility for the riot through it pursuit of policy
but the government did find a way of accepting a link between the riot and social problem without bringing it main policy into the debate namely by linking the growth of violent disorder to crime and drug
the emphasis on crime and the criminal act of the rioter in the official response to the riot took a general and a specific form
the general form relied on the argument that the riot were not a form of protest against the insufferable social condition of area or the action of the police but a criminal act or a cry for loot
this wa an argument put most succinctly by geoffrey dear chief constable of the west midland dear and by douglas hurd the home secretary in relation to handsworth
but it recurred a a theme in official and press response to the other riot
the specific form wa built upon the notion that the outbreak of violence in handsworth and brixton in particular wa brought about by drug baron who saw the police attempting to curb their activity and control their territory
numerous example of this line of argument can be found in dear report on handsworth and in press coverage during the riot
taking the specific argument about the role of drug and drug baron in stimulating the riot this seems to have served two purpose
first it distanced the riot from the social economic political and other grievance which had been linked to them by locating the cause outside the social problem of dweller and in the simple greed of the drug baron to accumulate loot
second just a dear image of a few hundred young black criminal wa used to explain what happened in handsworth the problem of drug wa used to explain what happened at a national level
the issue of drug provided an everyday image already a national issue through saturation medium coverage and public debate around which the police the home office and other institution could depoliticize the riot
responding to the handsworth event douglas hurd wa moved to argue forcibly that such event were senseless and reflected more on those who participated in them than on the society in which they took place the sound which law abiding people in handsworth heard on monday night the echo of which i picked up on tuesday wa not a cry for help but a cry for loot financial time september
the chief constable for the west midland geoffrey dear took this argument further by pointing out that the day before the riot a successful carnival had taken place with the support of local community leader
he drew the conclusion from this that the riot came like a bolt out of the blue guardian november
such language focused attention on the individual or group who were breaking the law committing criminal act and threatening the interest of the majority
potential application
overview
ian masser
given the extent to which geographic information management is application driven it is important to consider in some depth the characteristic of some potential application field
in the process it will be necessary to examine not only the extent to which geographic issue feature on the policy issue agenda in these field but also the institutional context which governs and the extent to which data are available for research and policy analysis purpose
question on data availability are likely to be particularly important where user are heavily dependent on secondary source
in situation of this kind provision governing access and format may exert powerful constraint on the use that can be made of these data
the first four chapter in this part examine issue relating to geographic information handling in term of four potential application field
the author were asked to review the current state of the art in their field with particular reference to the likely requirement of the future policy issue agenda in term of the demand that they make on geographic information management
author were also asked to evaluate critically the state of geographic information provision in term of the need of user and to consider the impact of user requirement on the development of geographic information handling methodology
in this way the chapter in this part present a number of perspective which essentially complement and amplify the discussion in the previous part
in this case however methodological issue are tackled from a largely user standpoint whereas in the previous part they were viewed a substantive problem in their own right
in effect the product of the discussion in both part is a matrix where the methodological issue are listed along one axis and particular application field on the other
figure summarizes the main feature of this matrix
there are important difference between the chapter in this part both in the nature of the demand that they make on geographic information and also in the relative importance that is attached to geographic criterion a against other issue by planner and in these field
the first three chapter dealing with environmental monitoring natural and technological hazard and settlement and infrastructure application make use of a very wide range of geographic information
a major feature of these application is the extent to which they involve overlay of a variety of information drawn from different source on a topographic map base
for this reason they make particularly heavy demand on current gi technology both because of the size of the data set and the diversity of the data structure that are involved
brown chapter on geodemographics discus an application field where primary data collected for operational purpose are typically evaluated in relation to secondary data derived from source such a the census of population
the range of data set involved and the demand that are made on gi technology in application of this kind are often more limited than those of previous application field
however this is offset by the demand that are made on spatial analysis and modelling methodology
rhind chapter on environmental monitoring and prediction discus the role of geographic information management in promoting sustainable development on a global scale in the context of the issue identified in the brundtland report
it point to the impact that the finding of global environmental research are likely to have on most sector of the uk economy
this contribution also indicates the wide variety of group that are involved in monitoring environmental change and draw attention to the role that the european community is increasingly playing in these effort
one of the example of work in progress discus research that ha been carried out for the european commission a part of the corine project
this highlight the challenge for research in a field categorized by a lack of data for some country varying definition and standard in use and unreasonably high user expectation
the chapter a a whole draw attention to a number of key methodological issue that are involved in environmental monitoring and prediction
these include the highly specialized nature of much of the technical analysis the limited capacity for checking the accuracy of many of the finding of this kind of research and the consequent need for the development of inference machine for extracting useful information from secondary and often proxy data
in chapter gatrell and vincent consider a wide range of natural and technological hazard including industrial hazard risk assessment hazardous waste disposal emergency planning natural hazard and environmental epidemiology
the substantive content of much of this research straddle the social environmental and mathematical science
to model the dispersal of a plume of toxic gas generated by a chemical explosion and it impact on the surrounding area for example an understanding of atmospheric dispersion model epidemiology and population distribution would be required
in application of this kind the author argue that geographic information management in general and gi in particular have an important role to play and they give a number of example from research in progress to illustrate the current state of the art in this field
the discussion of operational problem and prospect further amplifies many of the issue raised in preceding chapter particularly with respect to the problem caused by the dependency on secondary data source and the need for much more detailed geographic information to overcome some of the problem associated with linking data set
like most of the other contributor to this section gatrell and vincent see decision support system a a major area for future development in the geographic information management field
given that most gi are rather dumb system requiring intelligent very computer literate user managing natural and technological hazard mean that this knowledge base must be built into the system so that it can be utilized quickly by untrained user after a disaster ha taken place or in an emergency
the settlement and infrastructure field is also characterized by a wide range of user with a great diversity of interest
these include not only central and local government but also major utility company and transport supplier
according to shepherd these user share a common need for information on the amount capacity and condition of urban land transport network utility hospital school and other major communal facility
in addition to these data requirement such user are also interested in developing their capability for modelling the changing relationship between the supply and demand for infrastructure in the context of both public and private sector
shepherd more than any other contributor to this section draw attention to the extent to which current effort in the geographic information management field are constrained by the highly fragmented nature of both data supplier and user both in sectoral and spatial term the great diversity of data set in varying format and the difficulty presented by institutional factor such a copyright provision data ownership and the control of access to data
digital data occupy a central position in this application field and a number of example are given to illustrate the extent to which their development ha been hampered or facilitated in various country by the policy of the organization with responsibility for digital data provision
in chapter brown review the development of geodemographics from it origin in the social area analysis of u census tract data from onwards
he describes the feature of the four main system that are currently in use in the uk and illustrates their application with reference to example drawn from retail analysis and store location market research credit rating and target marketing
brown demonstrates the extent to which the growth of research activity in this field ha led to the emergence of improved cluster analytic method for the multidimensional classification of people according to the type of area in which they live
in the last part of this contribution brown identifies a number of priority for future research
like gatrell and vincent and shepherd before him he is concerned with the lack of detailed geographical information particularly in this case with reference to the year between census
spatial linkage also feature prominently in brown discussion which amplifies many of the point made in the earlier contribution from openshaw in chapter
the analysis point to the need for the development of a fuzzy geodemographics methodology which take account of the effect of different type of spatial error
other major research priority for the future in this application field are the development of technique to explore the factor affecting consumer choice
this is particularly important in a field where many of the demand made by user are highly specialized in nature
in summary then a fig show many of the issue raised by this review of geographic information handling in the four potential application field are essentially complementary to those discussed in the part on methodological development
spatial analysis feature particularly prominent on the research agenda relating to natural and technological hazard and geodemographics
question relating to data integration emerge a being particularly critical in term of environmental monitoring and settlement and infrastructure application
spatial linkage and question relating to spatial representation feature prominently in the settlement and infrastructure and geodemographics field
the evaluation of error propagation is a matter of considerable significance in the environmental monitoring and settlement and infrastructure field
finally in all application field the finding of the review above suggest that there is a need for improvement in user interface of all kind
this is particularly evident in the demand for the development of decision support system and modelling capability
such demand highlight the extent to which geographic information management must be regarded a a mean to an end rather than an end in itself when viewed from the standpoint of the need of planner and
the final chapter in this section round off the discussion of research with an examination of organizational issue that need to be taken account of in handling geographic information
campbell present a conceptual framework for the analysis of the organizational issue involved in the development and implementation of gi
this contribution cut across many of the question relating to particular application that were raised in preceding chapter and draw attention to the danger of neglecting institutional and personal consideration in practice
all too often a the experience of many mature application indicates technical and matter dominate the system development phase and technically elegant solution are devised which fail to take enough account of user need and capability
campbell discus the role of geographic information in organization and the process of gi diffusion drawing upon research from a variety of social science discipline
the finding of the analysis are summarized in two set of research question for all application field
in this way she set out a research agenda for research which serf a similar function to the spatial analysis research agenda set out by openshaw at the beginning of part two
environmental monitoring and prediction
david rhind
introduction

thus the algal bloom off the italian adriatic shore in is reckoned to have caused the holiday trade and local fisherman loss running into ten if not hundred of million of pound
more globally the brundtland report wced noted that in the day during which the world commission wa at work

the african drought put the life of million people at risk and may have killed million of them

a a consequence of these and other disaster of rapid and broadcasting of them and of the concerned action of many individual the environment is now moving fast up the political agenda patten

this chapter then attempt to review some of the problem in environmental monitoring and prediction describes some of the relevant scientific and organizational activity and look ahead to what is likely to happen next
the nature of environmental process
notwithstanding mr thatcher confidence that we can fix environmental problem the difficulty associated with a task even a apparently simple a monitoring a state variable are considerable
some of the reason for this the difficulty of deciding on appropriate proxy variable and on economical yet temporal and spatial sampling framework taking account of the relative importance of aperiodic and rare event a compared to process processing the vast volume of data usually involved and organizing the multidisciplinary and often multinational researcher involved are discussed briefly later
even at this stage however it is important to stress that we have a very incomplete understanding of many process in the natural environment
the next section therefore attempt to summarize what we do know it is derived chiefly from the earth system science committee essc
temporal and spatial scale of operation
even ignoring the effect of man earth system process operate at a variety of spatial and temporal scale see fig see also rosswall et al
thus microclimate effect can have major implication for local population such a those brought about by the photochemical smog of los angeles are often applicable only over area of a few hectare or le and may operate on a diurnal cycle
in contrast soil creation cf soil degradation may require hundred or thousand of year
in between are variation in phenomenon such a el nino
the sampling theorem indicates that we must sample these phenomenon at a frequency of no le than half their wavelength if we are to avoid bias in measurement
in this chapter the primary concern is with change occurring over time span from minute to century and from spatial wavelength from about m to about km
it is however impossible to separate out process acting at different scale and over different period a single volcanic eruption lasting hour or day sometimes lead to dust and gas being ejected into the atmosphere over a period of month and this in turn may lead to global climatic fluctuation over year or decade
conversely a and phenomenon such a the movement of tectonic plate can lead to local stress accumulation and to it release by an earthquake in a few second and with highly local effect
this therefore ha the following consequence

we should know something about the periodicity of the variable we are monitoring if we are not to risk either unnecessarily detailed data collection or aliasing of trend

since we know that the periodicity of some variable is longer than the monitoring already carried out by human being we must make use of surrogate or proxy variable to extend our range of knowledge such a via tree ring palynology oxygen isotope ratio from ice core and geomorphological evidence of environmental change

since we are not yet able to predict all the interaction which may be important in a study of environmental problem collecting potentially useful data a well a those believed central to the problem under study is often wise

we must accept that most data collection exercise will inevitably be a compromise on the ground of cost and hence le than perfect data set will be produced

irrespective of the use of surrogate monitoring environmental process only make sense over which are extended by human standard hence the igbp see below is designed to run for two or three decade

change in political priority may simply result in the need for informed guesswork if suitable data are not available
much attention will be given throughout this chapter to monitoring the environment on a global basis
this is not merely because of it topical nature
the main reason is that though some problem are local and are best studied that way many others even involving a limited geographical extent are best understood within a global framework
thus no meteorologist would attempt to forecast the weather or day ahead without using a mathematical model based on observation from all around the world
moreover recent work ha shown that much of the heat energy in the sea of the north atlantic every square kilometre of which give off a much energy a a nuclear power station and hence influence our weather is absorbed from sunlight in the tropical pacific and is carried by ocean current through the drake passage and up into the atlantic
thus to understand some local and many regional national and continental and all global environmental event we need to have a global perspective and hold global database rhind and mounsey mounsey and tomlinson
in no way however doe this invalidate the need for microscale study for instance while global data set may indicate the extent of algal bloom and may suggest cause of them only detailed study of the algae themselves can provide understanding of why the bloom is occurring
the process themselves
a major complication however is that the environment can rarely be treated a in a laboratory experiment
given this determining the nature of the interaction between the variable becomes a matter of major difficulty
figure is taken from essc and is an attempt to show the interaction between environmental process a well a the indicator and implication of change in the state of the environment
in essence the figure can be summarized a showing process within the physical climate system and within the biogeochemical one these system being interwoven by the global role of water and increasingly affected by human activity
the main component of the first system are well known the atmosphere is it engine and atmospheric circulation is driven by difference in solar heating between the equatorial and polar region
we are however becoming ever more aware of the massive influence of ocean on our climate research into interaction is now a priority
in ocean dynamic study important topic are heat storage circulation and the role of sea ice
atmospheric circulation and in turn precipitation and temperature is also greatly affected by the balance of thermal energy at the land surface itself affected by the vegetation and terrain characteristic
the biogeochemical system embrace the totality of the movement of the key element essential to life carbon nitrogen oxygen phosphorus and others through what ha been described a the total earth system
the ocean and their biota play a central role in the carbon and nutrient cycle global ocean circulation is also critical to the global carbon budget
trace gas in the atmosphere are key component of the cycle of such element a carbon nitrogen oxygen sulphur and the halogen a is now well known their concentration are much influenced by biogenic and anthropogenic activity and the concentration of such gas a carbon dioxide ozone methane nitrous oxide and the chlorofluoromethanes cfms strongly affect radiative transfer and provide a link with the physical climate system
a particular cause for concern is that the concentration of the two main cfms is increasing by about per cent per annum while the equivalent figure for methane nitrous oxide and carbon dioxide are and per cent
finally the chemistry of the stratosphere is dominated by the photochemical production and catalytic destruction of ozone
there are several important way in which biogeochemical process can influence climate and hence habitability except where the latter is maintained at enormous cost
if for instance the concentration of certain trace gas see above continue to increase it ha been predicted that the earth surface temperature will increase by an amount comparable to that since the last major phase of the most recent glaciation about year bp though there is some dispute about the magnitude of the likely change
the converse case the effect of physical climate change on biogeochemical process is also of obvious importance change in annual average and cycle of temperature and precipitation together with the probability of extreme event such a prolonged drought or frost are major determinant of terrestrial ecosystem type at least in area largely unaffected by human activity
change to the environment have increased rapidly a a consequence of growing population number and of numerous development in technology
fossil fuel combustion for instance ha led to increased concentration of sulphate in precipitation acid rain and many river lake and estuary have been greatly affected by phosphate from agricultural urban or industrial source
it should be stressed however that while the outline of human activity are clear there are still many uncertainty for instance we know that the atmospheric concentration of carbon dioxide ha risen about per cent since
but calculation of the total carbon released by fossil fuel combustion imply that if all such carbon remained in the atmosphere the concentration would have increased by twice a much
the absolute difference between the two figure seems to be due to two different factor absorption by the ocean and other reduction in carbon stock in living biota the latter being strongly affected by human activity since the industrial revolution
doe god play dice
much environmental prediction is predicated upon a logical positivist or newtonian deterministic basis
the environmental system are effectively regarded a machine whose working can all be discovered described in differential equation form and whose future activity can thus be predicted in detail if their initial state are known
an argument by many atmospheric physicist for example is that shortcoming in the accuracy of weather prediction over period of more than a few day largely result from the unsophisticated nature of existing model the lack of suitable data and inadequate computer power see fig derived from tyler
in contrast the advocate of chaos theory stewart argue that some natural system are so sensitive to tiny stimulus that even the faint beat of a butterfly wing could be the ultimate trigger for a hurricane
in essence they argue that tiny difference in the initial condition of many system can lead to widely different outcome since the system exhibit stochastic behaviour within a deterministic framework
if so there is little chance of making accurate forecast of these system
this ha been recognized by among others essc
the author of that report accepted that there is a theoretical limit of week in explicit prediction of fluctuation in weather because of the influence of turbulence within the dynamic such limit imply that medium and prediction must inevitably be stochastic
to complicate matter still further however it seems at least possible that the component of the earth system may best be predicted deterministically at some spatial and temporal scale but stochastically at others and that the basis of prediction will differ for different component
a an example atmospheric temperature show marked variability a strong seasonal cycle with some variation a weak minimum variability for year average and then increased variation again at longer essc
it need hardly be pointed out that coping with such multiple database on which modelling is to be carried out is not a trivial exercise
finally it is perhaps worth concluding this section by emphasizing that there is still much controversy among the scientific community about the magnitude of many of the effect being discussed
in general the research work of the international group of scientist including those involved in the committee and in the uk committee on global environmental change ha progressively reduced the magnitude of the predicted effect of for example global warming
in giving the robens coal science lecture at the royal institution sir john mason a former director of the meteorological office urged caution in interpreting the result of the massive atmospheric and oceanic modelling exercise a the equilibrium model are refined to take account of the thermal lag in ocean etc lower value of predicted change are likely
thus while almost all scientist are at the time of writing convinced from the evidence that change in climate is under way and that regional effect may be much greater than the global average the magnitude of the latter is now thought likely to be about half of what wa predicted only year ago
who is involved and what is going on
if we consider the environment in the broadest sense much monitoring of it ha been in progress for many year and by an enormous diversity of organization in the uk these include the doe the forestry commission the nature conservancy the health and safety executive local authority the component member of the natural environment research council such a the institute of terrestrial ecology and the british antarctic survey individual or research group in academia the cegb the friend of the earth and uk centre for economic and environmental development ceed
the diversity of monitoring organization seems just a great in other country numerous multinational organization both the un environment programme unep and the international union for the conservation of nature iucn and the international institute for environment and development iied are also active in the field
moreover commercial monitoring of the environment is now also routine notably to predict crop yield in the main area and hence facilitate the buying of future
the international scientific involvement
scientist have both promoted and responded to the increasing interest in the environment
thus at the global scale the international council of scientific union icsu ha endorsed the setting up of the international geosphere biosphere project igbp to describe and understand the interactive physical chemical and biological process that regulate the total earth system the unique environment it provides for life the change that are occurring in that system and the manner by which these change are influenced by human action report of ad hoc planning group for igbp quoted in igbp
priority in the igbp is intended to be given to those area which deal with key interaction and significant change on the of decade to century that most affect the biosphere that are most susceptible to human perturbation and those that will most likely lead to a practical predictive capability for global change
this is to be put into operation by concentrating on four theme

documenting and predicting global change

observing and improving our understanding of dominant forcing function

improving our understanding of interactive phenomenon in the total earth system

assessing those effect of global change which will be large scale and cause major modification to both renewable and resource
by igbp had progressed a far a defining a set of seven core project igbp addressing these four theme
in addition plan for regional research centre and for the data and information system for igbp known a had been announced
the latter are particularly relevant to this chapter
based in paris and working under professor rasool it is intended to concentrate on managerial and policy aspect of the task in the first year but then to expand considerably thereafter
task agreed for the include making available a directory of data directory modelled on nasa master directory providing data set for education and training and undertaking a land cover pilot study
until remarkably little interaction had taken place between the hard science and the social science community on global monitoring and prediction
it is noteworthy however that the royal society made a plea for just this type of multidisciplinary work in it submission on greenhouse gas to the house of lord select committee on science and technology royal society
fortunately in addition to the action of the world hard science community a parallel effort is now being initiated by social scientist fuchs jacobson and price
currently this is organized and sponsored by the international social science council issc the un university and the international federation of institute of advanced study
it objective are to

improve scientific understanding and increase awareness of the complex dynamic governing human interaction with the total earth system

study explore and anticipate social change affecting the global environment

identify broad social strategy to prevent or mitigate undesirable impact of global change or to adapt to change which are unavoidable

analyse policy option for dealing with global environmental change and promoting the goal of sustainable development
jacobson and price provide a useful summary of the way in which human factor contribute to and are affected by likely global change in particular they stress the importance of the issue and the role of gi in coping with some of the problem of data integration and manipulation
the issc proposed it own work programme in the human dimension of global change in late
while these organization intrinsically have a membership and are concerned with research into global environmental change others share the same interest but from a more restricted geographical base
a leading example of this is the european science foundation which ha sponsored research programme in both the physical and social science aspect of environmental change esf

some example of environmental monitoring project
the local scale
at the local scale it is usually impossible to neglect the effect of multiple process operating
an example of environmental modelling and prediction where the interaction between different process and dynamic feedback is taken into account is given by haber and schaller
their work formed part of one unesco man and biosphere mab project carried out in the berchtesgaden national park in bavaria
following holling and grossman they conceptualized the relationship at a series of hierarchical level

the lowest or process level is directly and usually obviously connected to perceived reality
thus process and interrelationship are mostly obvious simple and linear data are usually readily available and may be voluminous
this level is readily handled in commercial gi

the intermediate or dynamic level is concerned with le frequent and often irregular event a temporary lack of water because of fire frost or excessive demand from an increasing populace
characteristically the data used may be more difficult to obtain and are usually more spatially aggregated modelling software which permit feedback loop is essential

the top or strategic level is the most difficult to explore the external influence are often unpredictable by formal mean
relevant data are therefore difficult to identify and scenario building is one of the few approach available
the haber and schaller approach is to these different level and their accompanying approach using an ecological balance model
result of running this with different scenario include time slice map of possible outcome and of the exchange of material and energy within the study area
while ultimately qualitative it seems to offer a method for coping with different type of process and incorporating stochastic and truly random event
the national and continental scale the corine project
the corine programme represents the product of much activity by the european commission xi for the environment
it originates from an italian request to the council of minister in to identify environmentally balanced and unbalanced area in the community the first attempt to do this were unsuccessful and though by it wa clear that a new approach based on an environmental information system wa the most promising one funding for this wa not secured until
a experimental programme to collect and ensure the consistency of information on the state of the environment and natural resource in the european community wa set up and labelled corine
the objective of corine were to be achieved through bringing together existing data holding in the member state developing method for holding analysing and presenting the data and encouraging the exchange of data
a number of priority area were identified including biotopes of importance for nature conservation acid deposition and it effect on soil and biotopes and the protection of the environment of the mediterranean region briggs and martin
many achievement can be claimed by the corine project team
a a result of some involving all the member state and often several group within each one database of topography soil water resource and quality biotopes atmospheric emission climate soil erosion and administrative boundary have been built up for the whole community and can be interrelated other data set such a land cover derived from satellite imagery have already been compiled for some of the member state
various aspect of the corine project have been described in paper by rhind et al wiggins et al briggs and martin briggs and mounsey and cec
for the present purpose however the key finding are

many necessary data set were unavailable for reason of administrative inadequacy confidentiality constraint cost or in certain country

the unavoidable reliance upon existing data set led to many problem due to even of commonly used variable eight different definition of potential were in use in the member state and maximum temperature at each weather station wa defined in at least four different way

the compilation of a spatially coherent database from mapped information compiled by different organization at different scale and on different topographic base see rhind and clark is often difficult

user expectation are often unreasonably high use of administrative computing system encourages bureaucrat to believe that environmental data can just a readily be analysed and used to support decision
the fuzzy nature of much geographically distributed data the inherent error in it the effect of the processing algorithm used and the assumption of known interaction between variable ensures that completely routine use by unskilled user is unlikely to be possible in the foreseeable future

more detailed data are required for particular task a the role of corine grows
the european commission proposal for an environment agency see above will subsume the corine team and database
the global scale nasa and
without question the largest player in the global environment arena is nasa
the organization ha initiated many of the scheme which now are under discussion the igbp for instance ha been strongly influenced by nasa proposal
a summary of current activity and future plan is given in nasa
by way of example current programme are collecting global data on stratospheric ozone on and variable and on the earth radiation budget

in addition however funding ha recently been approved for a much more ambitious scheme the earth observing system eos
this is conceived not a a set of hardware but a a comprehensive information system focused on the need identified by the essc see above and anticipating somewhat those of igbp
it will collate data from the two proposed space station polar platform one european space agency platform a japanese one and also from the manned space station
on this basis a data flow of no le than terabyte byte day is anticipated by the
a major user of nasa data and skill ha been the un environment programme
formed in the wake of the stockholm conference unep soon spawned the global environment monitoring system gem a well a an international register of potentially toxic chemical and a global network of source to locate and provide technical scientific and management information on the environment
the need for a mechanism to handle the global environmental data wa defined in the early and the global resource information database grid resulted
mooneyhan ha described the progress of the pilot stage of grid which culminated in approval for a full operational phase grid is now involved in integrating storing and exploiting a variety of global environmental database mostly acquired from nasa
in addition to the work being carried out in the unep hq at nairobi and in the site in geneva a series of grid regional node are now being set up each equipped with the same hardware and software and local subset of the data
the first of these is in bangkok and another is to be opened in latin america
moreover national node are also being set up the recent ibm gift to grid see above ha ensured that powerful microcomputer have been installed in many african country together with national and continental data set
training of unskilled staff to operate this equipment and to exploit the scientific data is now a major role for grid staff
technical aspect and problem
it follows from much of the above that there are major challenge in use of environmental data
these are best considered by itemizing characteristic of contemporary environmental monitoring and prediction

the use of secondary data rather than primary data collected by the data analyst

the need at least with data on the terrestrial environment for an inference process to extract useful information from the secondary and often proxy data

the data volume collected are often voluminous even by the standard of contemporary computing facility

the analysis carried out are often arcane in detail to all but a small group of high priest

we have only a limited capacity for checking the accuracy of many environmental monitoring result let alone of prediction
some of these characteristic are now addressed in slightly more detail it will be obvious that such problem merit a paper in themselves
remote sensing a a data collection process
a the need for more extensive yet consistent and data becomes more pressing increased use of remote sensing seems inevitable
no other data collection methodology obviates the short distance variation in data set induced by variation in data collection and aggregation methodology typically encountered between adjacent nation state
the problem is now recognized especially in europe and strenuous effort are being made to harmonise the data set through the use of standard classification such a that for land use produced by the conference of european statistician in
at present however environmental data are far le than ideal
recognizing this nasa concluded that forthcoming global science project would need land surface altitude data at three resolution km resolution in xy and m resolution in z on a global basis m xy resolution and m resolution in z for regional database and m xy resolution and m in z for local study
they argued that existing map and digitized file from them are unable to meet these need at global or regional scale and only remote sensing could help in the short term the availability of stereometric data from the french spot satellite ha already led to proposal for automated creation of global digital elevation model with a spatial xy resolution of about m muller
for many terrestrial purpose however a substantial inference process must take place to convert the radiometric measurement into useful information in contrast more direct measurement of sea state etc are possible
the value of this information is inherently dependent upon the quality of the inference process and that in turn depends upon the complexity of the scene the spatial temporal and spectral resolution of the sensor and the particular algorithm used
thus far for instance accuracy of land cover let alone what is often needed land use determined from landsat and spot imagery for the uk have rarely been higher than per cent unless trivial classification land have been used
one solution to this is to densify the ground control and another is to use contextually based classifier rather than the traditional spectrally based one
but the ground condition in some part of europe make good result extremely difficult to obtain some area of portugal for instance have field size of only a few metre and exhibit and cropping
a further difficulty is the cost of the data in relation to it anticipated benefit
relatively few study have yet been carried out except in such area a crop prediction and ocean navigation where they are generally shown to be highly advantageous in saving someone else money
it may be that a study commissioned from contractor by the british national space centre will provide useful evidence on the cash value of remote sensing it is particularly timely in view of the appointment of professor pearce see above a the adviser to the uk secretary of state for the environment
other work on assessment of cost and benefit of such data have been carried out for the french government by professor didier
finally since data are often costly to acquire it follows that summary of them the state of the european environment report cec and the environmental data report of the un ep gem marc are of considerable value
equally the signposting role now being adopted by unep grid project which is expected to offer access to a catalogue of environmental data set and detail of the responsible agency in is to be welcomed
the data problem and partial solution
the lack of harmonization of definition and method of collection of environmental data have already been outlined above
in the european community of nation state for instance no le than eight procedure for calculating potential have been in use
the need for harmonization is obvious and in this respect must follow from the successful pioneering achievement of eurostat in harmonizing the definition in trade demographic and other social science statistic see cec
an additional and severe problem is that the volume of data which are already collected are huge by the standard of only a decade ago
by they will be very much greater notably from the eos programme
nasa ha announced plan to collect up to terabyte byte day
since remote sensing data set especially those pertaining to terrestrial area of the globe typically need much to calibrate transform and then perform an inference process and hence convert measurement of the radiation reflected or emitted by small area of ground into useful land cover data the processing power required is going to be formidable
other data set are smaller in volume but more complex in structure and in their characteristic
to hold all of the scale topographic map coverage alone for the european community would probably require about terabyte of storage
parenthetically the form in which the data may be held can affect dramatically the scale of the problem faced
it would be technically possible for instance to hold in le than terabyte detailed information for every individual in the world akin to that collected about everyone in the uk through the census of population
in practice legislation generally forbids such data being held thus and distributed in anything other than area aggregate form the commonly employed to give table of population number broken down by age and sex often result in a great multiplication of the data volume
this all present major problem of data storage handling especially for global data set display and dissemination
fortunately technical development have ensured that the increase in computing power per unit cost ha been growing at about an order of magnitude every year over the last three decade
indeed this may grossly the present situation the rapid spread of system seems to facilitate competition and at the time of writing performance of workstation per unit cost seems to be increasing at about per cent per annum
moreover the advent of device like may well make substantial data set available even to those with modest computing power a for instance can hold about megabyte byte can be reproduced currently for about and read on a device costing about
yet despite such revolutionary change in technology novel solution will still be required to make effective use of the new data set
one such solution is goodchild and yang scheme for a hierarchical spatial data structure to handle data for the spherical earth
a particular problem is that little or no quantitative regard ha been paid until recently to the effect of quality variation in environmental data
the literature of the last few year is thronged with paper proposing that these must be taken into account but with few realistic proposal on how this is to be achieved
goodchild ha made perhaps the best summary of the problem and possible solution to date
finally relatively little emphasis ha been given to the management of data a a corporate resource available to a wide community many environmental data are collected on a basis and lost once the urgency of the initial research is over
however the report of the data and facility working group of the uk committee on global environmental change argued strongly that planning for the dissemination and maintenance of such data wa a vital role
it also noted that ownership of and access to environmental data wa a policy matter of the greatest importance this may be more difficult in within country data than with global data since the latter are often already the subject of international exchange agreement at zero cost
global environmental research and the social science
thus far the emphasis ha been very much on the natural science aspect of environmental monitoring and prediction
that is unremarkable since the anticipation of such problem and assessment of some of their cause and magnitude can only be made by environmental scientist
yet the consequence of any significant change are a matter of the utmost concern to planner and to politician at all level the quantification of the cost and benefit of alternative policy strategy is very much a matter for economist and the adaptation of society to massive change is a particular interest to sociologist and others
for geographer who span the conventional and now archaic dichotomy between the natural and the environmental science all of these aspect need to be woven together to anticipate the likely spatial pattern of the effect of massive change the redistribution in trade health and wealth which they will bring about and the knock on effect these consequence themselves will have on society and the environment
for social scientist then environmental monitoring and prediction are a matter of considerable significance especially a globalization of market and economy proceeds
the economic and social research council esrc commissioned two report on global environmental change to guide or at least inform the allocation of research funding
these report pearce turner may be taken a informed view from at least the economist in the uk social science community on the social science aspect of global environmental change
pearce for instance presented an economist view of the topic for research a follows

the theory and practice of international agreement viewed in a game theory context

the theory of optimal behaviour under scientific uncertainty

framework especially for dealing with climatic effect

definition of the impact of climate change on eastern europe and the developing country

appropriate policy on dioxide greenhouse gas

assessment of the ecological value of tropical forest

economic instrument for reducing greenhouse gas

the international politics of climate change

national and global energy option given the greenhouse effect

trade and global change
turner argued that the priority are a follows

the consequence of rise

technique for the valuation of environmental resource and effect

an assessment of management tool institutional adaptation and policy integration in regard to global environmental change

study of agriculture in relation to climate change

understanding of how environmental issue and technical change interact

the interrelationship between environmental ethic and economics
there is then no shortage of social science research which is claimed to be necessary if we are to cope with environmental change
some of it is being carried out in march esrc announced a programme of research on global environmental change
however perhaps most critical of all in the early stage is social science practice rather than research
in the usa at least there need to be an improvement in scientist understanding of how to influence the allocation of funding for remedial measure or for further research see kitsos and ashe
all too often it seems that the coupling of an a yet imperfect scientific understanding to is tenuous see table
fortunately considerable work ha already begun on the legal political and institutional aspect of global environmental change see for instance nitze
what next
the content of this chapter have scarcely touched upon such important environmental research a the world ocean climate experiment or the world climate research programme
nor ha there been any discussion of the growing requirement in the uk a elsewhere to carry out an environmental impact assessment for all major development
the consequence for some nation or subgroup in a population of being without access to environmental data or the tool for analysing them while others have such access are potentially profound a the european commission ha recognized in issuing a directive on public access to environmental data cec yet space limitation have also precluded their discussion
despite these shortcoming dictated by the space available what ha been said should be sufficient to illustrate the enormous and diverse scope of environmental monitoring and prediction
such is it diversity that measuring the total expenditure on it seems quite impossible and the number of actor already involved is vast
what is clear however is that monitoring is rarely a simple exercise that the of the sponsor of monitoring and environmental research are rarely long term though most science is inevitably of this nature and that the increasingly multinational nature of such work necessitates a degree of management not always present in local or nationally based scheme
in these circumstance it is scarcely surprising that there is evidence of international and interdisciplinary dispute a terney ha chronicled in regard to igbp
moreover a newby ha pointed out the complexity of environmental research have created a new kind of relationship between research and policy in the past the relationship wa predicated on the belief that science provided with objective hard fact on which to base their soft policy
but now we find scientist delivering only soft uncertain fact to facing hard decision
yet even if all of this cause great uncertainty among scientist it is still a reasonable prediction that a decade ahead will see both environmental monitoring and prediction treated a an everyday need and activity in major organization
we shall also see the existence of binding requirement upon national government certainly in the european community to collect at least basic environmental indicator in a harmonized form cec
more than that it seems highly likely that the social science aspect of environmental problem will underpin the action of government and international agency
perhaps the single most important conclusion to be drawn from this review is that the monitoring modelling and management of the global environment are task which uniquely require the integration of skill and technique from many discipline
building such research team is essential
underlying it all however is one obvious fact that the gathering and analysis of geographically distributed environmental data form the necessary for ensuring the success of our future on earth
