managing natural and technological hazard
anthony gatrell and peter vincent
introduction
few area of the application of gi technology can be a socially significant or environmentally relevant a the management of emergency and disaster due to natural and technological hazard
whether attempting to construct a database of resource for use in planning response to nuclear emergency developing optimal route for scheduling the safe transport of hazardous substance or monitoring the health implication of a disaster gi can assist in identifying possibility and formulating solution
the have been declared the international decade for natural disaster reduction
let u hope that can in some small way help mitigate the suffering and hardship felt by all those afflicted by the effect of hazard which a we have learnt with bitter recent experience in the uk can occur in an untimely fashion in the most improbable of place
research on hazard is multidisciplinary and straddle the social environmental and mathematical science
if for instance we wish to model the dispersal of a plume of toxic gas resulting from a chemical explosion ass it possible impact on human health and evaluate likely evacuation scenario of the population at risk we would require for example a knowledge of atmospheric dispersion model epidemiology and population distribution
some researcher suggest that hazard and emergency that might result can be regarded a either natural or technological
we shall elaborate on this simple division below but suggest here that the wealth of literature on the former see for instance burton et al and perry ha yet to be matched by a similar volume of work on the latter
there are sign that this imbalance is being rectified zeigler et al
hazard research like few other gi application area is not only stretching the present technology to it limit but is a quite remarkable focus of international effort into several important area such a expert system and simulation study
in this sense the scene is clearly one of hazard problem looking for improved gi rather than for gi looking for good problem a is all too often the case
hazard research
what are hazard
formally a hazard can be defined a a physical situation with a potential for human injury damage to property damage to the environment or some combination of these health and safety executive
a hazard is a threat which given a set of circumstance may become translated into a realized event
what we choose to call this event depends upon factor such a it magnitude we speak for instance of accident emergency disaster and catastrophe each of which carry connotation concerning the scale of the event and each of which will have a set of human environmental consequence
on march one of the most powerful volcanic disturbance this century the bezymianny eruption occurred
few people noticed the event a it took place in an uninhabited part of kamchatcka and caused no known casualty
in contrast the extrusion of a small volume of lava from a secondary cone on the slope of tristan da cunha became the focus of global interest when during october the island lobster processing plant wa smothered and the people of the island only settlement were evacuated to the uk
these two contrasting event emphasize the central fact that even natural hazard are not defined solely by the characteristic of the event but by the interaction of those event with the human occupation of the threatened area
a noted above the simple division of hazard is between those which are natural and those which are technological or
each of these may be further subdivided and the typology shown in fig draw upon the classic work of burton and kates in separating geophysical from biological hazard and zeigler et al in distinguishing public or what we might call societal hazard from private individual one
the further subdivision of natural hazard is a is that of individual technological hazard
zeigler divide the public hazard into those which result from the production of raw material and manufactured good those which originate in transport and transmission and those which threaten the public in their role a consumer
the united nation disaster relief organization undro ha produced a classification of disaster derived on the basis of case data table
undro recognizes three basic type of disaster accident natural event and other disaster
the differentiation of accident from other type is useful in the context of emergency planning and is not so clearly conveyed by other hazard typology
however the temptation in all classification exercise is to produce partitional scheme and this should really be resisted here
it is more useful johnson to adopt a scheme fig that recognizes for instance food poisoning a both a personal and consumer hazard or lead pollution from car exhaust a both a meteorological event and technological hazard both public and private
an air crash a at lockerbie affect an entire community directly a well a being an occupational hazard and risk to the individual traveller
hillslope failure a at aberfan in south wale in is a geomorphic hazard but may arise because of raw material extraction
dutch elm disease is a floral hazard but is exacerbated by the transport of infected log
hohensemer et al make the important point that hazard are multidimensional in nature and suggest dimension along which any hazard may be scored see table
these factor will of course be important in deciding on the role that gi can play in hazard monitoring and emergency planning
for instance some event will persist briefly have immediate consequence minor transgenerational effect and have little or no potential for mortality an air crash is an example
others such a a chemical explosion involving the release of a toxic gas may persist for a week or more have delayed consequence may affect a future generation if the toxic chemical is mutagenic and may have a significant impact on plant and animal population
there may be more scope for a gi approach in the latter than in the former situation
the hohensemer scheme is not however beyond criticism
for example can hazard really be thought of a having any intentionality
industrial hazard and risk assessment
once hazard have been identified there may follow effort to ass the hazard risk
by risk we understand the likelihood of a specified undesired event occurring within a specified period or in specified circumstance health and safety executive
it may of course be easier to quantify risk for natural hazard because of historical record and statistical estimation of recurrence interval
technological hazard are more unpredictable and may be extremely rare so that it becomes difficult to use probability concept to quantify risk especially those which rely on notion of relative frequency
the identification of chemical hazard requires that the location of site be known together with the dangerous substance stored or processed there
in the uk see petts for a splendid overview the health and safety executive must be notified of site where hazardous substance in excess of threshold limit are handled
such substance and threshold include for instance tonne of flammable liquid petroleum gas and the explosive sodium chlorate and tonne of toxic chlorine gas
some installation are notifiable along with thousand of kilometre of pipeline mostly natural gas transmission line
following a number of major accident involving industrial activity including those at flixborough humberside in beek the netherlands in and seveso and manfredonia in italy in the ec issued a directive on major accident hazard
the directive which is commonly referred to a the seveso directive wa issued in june and in the uk it requirement were embodied in the control of major accident hazard cimah regulation
among other thing these regulation require operator of hazardous installation to draw up and emergency plan and to give information to member of the public who live or work near such installation houston
there are presently about cimah site
however many potentially hazardous chemical installation are not covered by such regulation
clearly a plant which store tonne le than is required for notification slip through the net while large number of handling site warehouse for instance are not covered
the regulation have obvious implication for work a illustrated below
in halton borough cheshire for instance there are notifiable installation with over people living within the defined consultation zone petts
it is also relevant to point out here the work of the health and safety executive in developing technique for quantitative risk assessment health and safety executive
such technique include the use of a risk assessment tool riskat input to which include data on wind direction and speed the output of which is a map of calculated risk contour
in societal risk assessment it is also necessary to input data on the distribution of population around the installation
this can be a difficult and process and inevitably some simplifying assumption are needed health and safety executive
again the implication are clear and are discussed below
hazardous waste disposal
the disposal of both nuclear and waste ha proved to be of major public concern in recent year
the rather clumsy handling by nirex of the search for site to store and waste together with very recent worry about the import of toxic waste such a polychlorinated biphenyls pcbs are but two example of such concern in the uk
however while the former ha been given considerable attention by geographer summarized by openshaw et al there ha been relatively little such work in the uk on the disposal of waste
this contrast with the situation in the usa greenberg and anderson where the of abandoned site is a priority
certainly in term of the volume of waste generated in the uk hazardous industrial waste should be high on the environmental agenda while le than million tonne of all nuclear waste were generated in time that amount were generated of hazardous waste openshaw et al
attention should be drawn to the three annual report of the hazardous waste inspectorate now merged with other branch of the doe to form her majesty inspectorate of pollution
these contain some valuable material on disposal practice and volume of waste generated and disposed of by each waste regulation authority wra county in england district in wale scotland and northern ireland
each wra is required to produce a waste disposal plan and these are starting to appear
they too contain useful material on for instance the location of site though individual site licence must be consulted for detail of what each is permitted to take in the way of hazardous waste
what is not known is information on the location of former site at which quite toxic material may have been dumped though recent work by egger in austria ha mapped a vast number of such site
it is these rather than existing licensed site which should be a focus of research activity particularly when examining possible link to ill health
we simply do not have enough evidence yet to back up the claim that people are almost certainly ill dead or dying because of these sloppy waste disposal activity openshaw et al
research is in progress however to ass possible health effect of poor incineration diggle et al
particular attention should be focused on hospital incinerator since these have been subject to crown immunity for many year and most are technically to burn at sufficiently high temperature for adequate disposal of waste gatrell and lovett
we need to produce an inventory of all such site together with a publicly available comprehensive database on all site accepting hazardous industrial waste
emergency planning
it is convenient to retain the distinction when discussing the background to emergency planning
nuclear emergency planning in the uk ha been reviewed by matthew and pepper
nuclear power station must prepare a plan and submit this to the nuclear installation inspectorate and health and safety executive for approval
evacuation plan are required to cover an area within a distance of km these detail the role to be played by the emergency service
the very narrow emergency planning zone contrast with those in the usa collins where planning is required up to km from the site to cover exposure to radiation plume
local authority in the uk that have declared themselves have been highly critical of british planning calling for an extension of emergency zone to at least km
zeigler et al should be consulted for material relating to evacuation behaviour in the wake of the incident at three mile island
in the uk little work of any description seems to have been done on human behaviour in the aftermath of release of hazardous substance nor is much available on public attitude to emergency planning
indeed no major study of evacuation due to hazard have been undertaken in recent time and this is a widely recognized deficiency which no research funding body seems willing to rectify
in the usa on the other hand a good deal of useful research in these area ha been undertaken
this research is brought together in very useful report produced by the oak ridge national laboratory tennessee sorenson et al vogt and sorenson and the disaster research centre university of delaware
perry ha written an interesting book on emergency planning and evacuation covering both natural and technological hazard
for him comprehensive emergency planning and management involve prevention protection response and restoration
by prevention we understand the elimination or reduction in risk perhaps by adequate zoning or safe routeing of shipment for instance
included in protection are method for detecting likely hazard event and in warning those likely to be affected
response includes search and rescue including the need to cope with secondary threat such a contamination of water supply after an explosion or fire following an earthquake
a perry and others have noted relatively few resource are devoted to the first two aspect the bulk going to response and restoration rebuilding
it should be clear from this brief description that these issue are inherently geographical
in one of the few study of evacuation behaviour after a hazard event liverman and wilson give weight to this argument
in a train carrying chlorine liquid petroleum toluene and propane wa derailed in mississauga ontario causing a series of explosion
this led to the evacuation of people which although staggered over several day led to great pressure on transport artery
an important finding wa that many relied on their own transport and went to stay with friend and relative some distance away rather than relying on the official evacuation reception centre
despite this the evacuation wa successful partly because the accident occurred at a weekend and the immediately affected area wa sparsely populated
in addition the police were well prepared stimulated largely by implementing a plan designed more to cope with an emergency at the nearby toronto international airport than for the event in question
it is not without interest to note that in the usa there is a federal emergency management agency fema established in charged with dealing with all type of emergency planning and management
in the uk there is no equivalent though the spate of disaster in the past year involving over life lost ha led to several call for such a national body to be established
natural hazard
in this short space it is not possible to go into any depth on the nature of particular natural hazard but only to highlight those aspect relevant to gi
needle to say the study of natural hazard is important a statement brought into sharp focus by the fact that natural hazard account for up to per cent of total death in the world each year mitchell
in for example more than people died in the cyclone and flooding of bangladesh and in the hurricane david and frederick caused more than damage in the usa
shah made a comprehensive investigation of natural disaster report for the period and concluded that both disaster frequency and magnitude measured in term of life lost are increasing
high death toll are still a characteristic of le developed country
surprisingly fog is the third most important hazard in europe after flood and volcano
research on natural hazard ha a long tradition in geography going back more than half a century
much of the impetus for such research arose in the usa from observation on river basin management and the need to reduce flood damage
the vast majority of natural hazard study have ignored the physical nature of the event per se and have concentrated on behavioural issue such a the perception and estimation of hazard
this emphasis is partly due to the background of the researcher involved many are human geographer and sociologist and partly because it is only really since the second world war that major hazard have been monitored systematically culminating of course in the last decade or so in the use of satellite technology
brief reference to two example of natural hazard may illustrate the potential relevance of a gi approach application of which are considered below
jones et al have examined the distribution of some landslide in the uk
their map show clearly an increased propensity for landsliding in the north and west of the uk
more to the point however is the fact that this distribution can be modelled in term of slope rainfall rock type and so on
in other word the actual hazard distribution can be understood and area at risk identified
the potential benefit to insurance company engineer and planner are clear
second a winter hazard in the uk with marked spatial localization is fog
predictive model of it distribution have clear implication for road and air safety
perry describes a fog potential index that is a function of local topography environmental feature affecting fog formation and distance from standing water body
reliance is currently placed on a network of monitoring station often sparsely located and frequently outside area gi could implement a predictive model based on digitized map feature and indeed the model could also be used in site allocation study for airport and the like
the majority of natural hazard research ha focused on single hazard but of course any area may be prone to more than one hazard type
this idea led hewitt and burton to develop the concept of
to achieve this they concentrated on the whole spectrum of damaging event in an area and explored their aggregate impact
the implication for gi in the development of hazardousness index are obvious and if data are available there is the potential to produce a variety of probability map
the collection of historical data on natural hazard is important since it is clear that their spatial pattern varies through time
many area that appear to be on current map may merely by passing through a temporary period of quiescence
this is perhaps best illustrated with reference to earthquake
for example in the whole of southern england wa affected by an earthquake whose epicentre wa located in what is now belgium a good deal of minor structural damage wa inflicted morse
presumably the builder of the channel tunnel are aware of this
environmental epidemiology
this is of course a vast subject area embracing the impact of the natural and technological environment on human health
it cover for instance the association between water and air pollution and ill health link between geological and pedological environment and ill health a well a association between specific technological hazard power line and possible health effect
we can only consider a small fraction of this work here little consideration is given to occupational environment for instance
in the uk such research is widespread though there are specialist environmental epidemiology research institute at southampton and cardiff funded by the medical research council and others at the university of surrey robens institute and at the london school for hygiene and tropical medicine
the latter house the small area health statistic research unit sahsru which ha a specific remit to conduct research into morbidity and mortality at local scale elliot
the sahsru liaises closely with opcs
the kind of database used by these group are discussed below
greenberg and a collection of paper in greenberg review some of the literature on environmental epidemiology
it seems worth stating at the outset that there are two way geographical research in this general area can proceed
one is to collect morbidity and mortality data usually the latter is more widely available though the former more useful and to examine spatial distribution for clustering
this ha itself generated a substantial literature see the paper in elliot for an overview and is nowhere better exemplified than in openshaw geographical analysis machine see ch
we then search retrospectively for evidence of possible environmental association
an alternative approach is to begin by hypothesizing an environmental determinant of ill health and to collect data to test an explicit hypothesis
if an association is suggested then we would want to collect data in other area to ass the hypothesis further
of course these two approach are not in practice in many case the hypothesis of interest will have themselves been generated by inductive mapping
one example of an hypothesis which ha been given serious attention in recent year is the possible link between electromagnetic field generated by power line or supply cable and ill health
some work perry et al suggested association with mental illness and suicide while others wertheimer and leeper have examined link to various cancer including leukaemia
a good bibliography is provided in perry and pearl
the central electricity generating board now privatized and split into two company is funding a project to ass link to childhood cancer while another recently announced study aim to look at link to sudden infant death
one obvious problem with implication for any gi input is that the effect are highly localized with little measurable field effect more than a few dozen metre away from the route
accuracy of digital data collection either of the power line or residential location is paramount
there seems to be a growing interest in examining association between ill health and the geological environment
gi work in this field matthew is reviewed later but we note here the work of the applied geochemistry group at imperial college responsible for a series of atlas on regional geochemistry and the existence of a society for environmental geochemistry and health
one area of recent debate concern radon gas and it link to lung cancer
this is taken very seriously in the usa where the environmental protection agency estimate that death from lung cancer each year are due to radon gas exposure
estimate from scandinavia suggest that per cent of such death are caused by exposure to radon richardson
the gas is trapped in house and is produced by the decay of uranium in rock and soil thus it ha been measured at high concentration in part of cornwall and devon
there are great difficulty in assessing health effect however since exposure varies greatly from house to house within small neighbourhood
carefully designed study are therefore required to measure the separate effect of radon exposure after controlling for smoking behaviour and other risk factor
other health concern which might merit attention by those involved in the regional research laboratory rrl initiative include air and water pollution
the debate about lead pollution from vehicle exhaust emission is well known le publicity ha been given to pahs polychlorinated aromatic hydrocarbon a product of combustion process and known to be carcinogenic lioy and daisey
research at the north west regional research laboratory nwrrl aim to create buffer around busy road and junction and to use data from the cancer registry to examine possible link between proximity to such source of pollution and prevalence of lung cancer
those with an interest in health and air pollution should note the availability of a very detailed database from the warren spring laboratory containing detail of smoke and sulphur dioxide emission at a large number of site in the uk
the possible link between nitrate in water and stomach cancer is the subject of much debate beresford a is the association between aluminium content and alzheimer disease
the problem of assessing such link are of course huge but there is scope for a contribution
the role of gi in hazard management scenario example
a we have already implied gi ha a role to play in all aspect of hazard research from hazard monitoring risk assessment and emergency planning to coping with an event and evaluating it consequence
the example described below illustrate all these though a yet there do not appear to be many instance of disaster in the management of which gi ha played a significant part
technological hazard emergency planning and gi
a considerable amount of research ha been undertaken to apply gi method to evacuation scenario around hazardous site
much of this research ha concentrated on network analysis of the road system
reference wa made above to cimah site major hazardous installation for which and emergency plan must be prepared
early research at the nwrrl focused on developing a gi for use by the police and county emergency planning officer in cumbria that would aid in the management of a possible explosion at a chemical factory in whitehaven west cumbria vincent et al dunn
the police required a portable system that could be implemented on an microcomputer
this wa written at the nwrrl using fortran and the graphical kernel system
the gi is and is exceptionally pl
it open with an outline map and the superimposition of the rather rigid zone used by the emergency planner
full zoom facility are available at any stage
in any emergency it is of course vital to have data on the distribution of population and resource
the system incorporates digitized data on the distribution of all domestic and property in the town together with digitized road data
both set of data were provided by pinpoint analysis ltd who are undertaking this digitizing task for the entire country
other spatially referenced data incorporated into the system include those on the distribution of school medical and transport service which can be displayed and supplementary information about them obtained
the gi permit population estimate to be made for any arbitrary rectangular region on the map
most significantly it incorporates a shortest path algorithm which us the road network to find optimal route between start and end node
although predating the rrl initiative by several year and indeed the emergence of gi a a major research area we should remind ourselves of openshaw work on appraising nuclear reactor site
using what would now be called gi skill openshaw examined over km grid square in the uk which intersect the coastline and related these to data from the census which were made available for such grid square
he demonstrated that there is an abundance of remote site in contrast to the official view that such site were increasingly hard to find
he suggested that in early spatial search for site only a small number were ever identified in the first place because rigorous search could not be performed by manual mean with poor quality data openshaw
heywood and cornelius have shown how gi can be used for monitoring possible radiation release and thus the relevance of gi in nuclear emergency planning and monitoring
they propose a national radiological spatial information system and in a pilot project in cumbria have integrated several layer of data within to show what this might involve fig
such data include those from the population and agricultural census a well a point data from rain gauge site and radiation monitoring station
a an example the system is used to determine restriction zone for the movement of sheep after the explosion at chernobyl in
this is done by finding area of high rainfall and parish with high sheep population
the map overlay of point and area information show generally good agreement with the restriction zone imposed by the ministry of agriculture fishery and food with the exception of a small area to the of cumbria bordering on lancashire
the british government carried out a review of it arrangement for handling nuclear accident overseas following the chernobyl accident
the doe through her majesty inspectorate of pollution hmip wa given the task of a national response plan installing the radiation monitoring network and acting a lead government department in an emergency hmso
the monitoring network ha become known a the radioactive incident monitoring network rimnet and ha a it prime responsibility the detection of abnormal increase in radiation level within the uk of the kind that might arise from an overseas nuclear accident
the full implementation of the rimnet system will take some time
by the end of gamma radiation dose monitor had been installed at meteorological station a part of phase of the development programme
radiation reading are taken every hour at each station and are transmitted to a central computer which analysis the data
the current criterion for alert is two reading of more than three time normal background either successively at the same site or simultaneously at two adjacent site
the dissemination of information in the event of an incident is dealt with at three level the first is the normal system of press notice the second is the use of teletext and viewdata ceefax and prestel to get direct to member of the public at their home or place of work the third is the use of telecom gold electronic mail to get more technical detail to various official body such a water authority jackson
phase of the rimnet scheme will be completed by the end of when between and monitoring site will have been established
given very wide regional and local variation in deposition question must be raised about the effectiveness of such a small network local authority will need to supplement it with their own network
there are important analytical problem to be addressed concerning the siting of such monitoring equipment and these are elaborated on later
abroad kaspar ha discussed a exercise with gi overtone involving the simulated evacuation of the population living in the vicinity of the neckarwestheim nuclear power plant in baden
in the scenario he outline an area affected by radioactive release is determined the population within that area is allocated to reception area with capacity constraint evacuation route are identified and traffic restriction implemented
little detail is provided however and it is thus difficult to evaluate his work fully
dangermond describes the use of the network module for use in emergency planning situation
he describes how a road network is digitized and subsequently analysed using allocation districting and routeing algorithm
allocation determines which arc in the network will be allocated to a particular node or centre districting make it possible to outline rapidly set of polygon in order to define specific area of interest district and to summarize their characteristic routeing provides a minimum path algorithm through the network the arc of which can be assigned weight according to road condition road capacity and so on
dangermond give several example in his paper including the use of network for the allocation of emergency vehicle optimum routeing of fire engine from garage to the accident scene and the movement of spill through sewer and river network
when combined with the other facility in quite complex disaster management scenario can be handled
for example earthquake fault zone can be combined with data on housing density and structural detail to predict earthquake damage level and these data then related to the network model
vincent illustrates the use of and it network module for finding safe route for chlorine transhipment on the road and rail system of england pl
in this case population density data for a km buffer on either side of network arc were overlaid on the network itself so a to act a weight for the minimum path algorithm
chosen route were those which minimized population rather than distance
hazardous waste disposal
there can be little doubt that a gi approach ha wide applicability in all sort of location problem where the goal is to minimize rather than a conventionally maximize accessibility to a population
a particularly good application is to the search for potential site for the disposal of nuclear and but none the le hazardous waste
we discus here some relevant work on the siting of facility for the disposal of nuclear waste before examining those for waste
the major contribution to informed debate about the search for site for the disposal of nuclear waste ha come from a group of geographer openshaw et al and a gi approach to this problem can pay high dividend
the work of carver see openshaw et al ch is an interesting example
one advantage is the ability to model a range of alternative by allowing particular criterion to enter or be omitted from the polygon overlay operation
conceptually what is offered is little more than an automated sieve mapping that planner have used for many year but the whole procedure is speeded up by many order of magnitude using gi software
the author examine both site and deep repository which use more restricted population criterion and allow offshore location to enter
data layer include geological map conservation area transport route petrochemical facility and demographic data
a different layer are added sequentially we see how the proportion of available land shrink pl for instance when geological criterion are set in the search for a deep repository per cent of land area remains and the addition of the population density layer reduces this to per cent
however adding a proximity to transport constraint lower this to per cent and so on
we can not pretend gi is a solution to the political problem of negotiation and justification but at the very least the openness of the procedure go some way towards satisfying a worried public
gi research into site selection for hazardous waste ha been almost exclusively conducted in north america and ha yet to be matched in the uk
jensen and christiansen working in the usa use a raster approach with a pixel resolution of m and boolean overlay to weed out particular site such a those which are poorly drained environmentally sensitive or inaccessible see also stewart
environmental monitoring of site for the disposal of toxic waste is of particular concern in the usa
the comprehensive environmental response compensation and liability act cercla legislation of superfund requires the cleaning up of the worst landfill site of which some had been identified by the environmental protection agency by foresman
a major worry ha been the threat posed by groundwater pollution and some research ha been conducted on using gi to monitor this merchant et al barringer et al von braun
this is an important topic since per cent of rural household in the usa consume only groundwater while half the u population consumes at least some groundwater merchant et al
clearly the research demand access to exceptionally good environmental data usually in three dimension
a foresman suggests we might expect remote sensing technology to play a major role
merchant et al for example use the image processing system erdas to construct an index of vulnerability to groundwater pollution this us variable such a depth to water table soil type slope and so on see estes et al for a similar approach
barringer et al overlay data on soil type and geology with that of groundwater quality hardness and corrosivity measure and build a linear model which show that the background environmental variable are good predictor of the water quality index
again a approach is used
a further example is work by von braun who us pmap to look at exposure of organic and metallic compound in groundwater in the vicinity of tucson airport arizona
using plume model that predict the movement of contaminant she is able to intersect the result with data on current well location and to ass which water supply area are worst contaminated
overlaying the result with residential location data provides map delineating exposure for each residence in each von braun
in principle it is then possible to compare such dos with epidemiological data once again indicating a link from a hazard event to assessment of health outcome
attention should be drawn to foresman comment that the u geological survey usgs at the eros data centre have successfully linked to a model of groundwater flow foresman
this kind of link between gi and other modelling program is to be warmly welcomed and parallel work at the nwrrl in linking gi and air pollution plume model
natural hazard and disaster management
several study in recent paper have shown the effectiveness of gi in mitigating the effect of major natural hazard
berke and ruch for example describe a gi for assessing the impact of hurricane on the texas gulf coast
hurricane damage through high wind and tidal surge cause an immense amount of destruction and pose a major threat to many coastal community in the usa
it ha been estimated for example that during the mid some million u citizen were subject to hurricane wind of over and million were subject to hurricane surge brinkman
the system described by berke and ruch is and ha an interesting modelling component called slosh sea lake and overland surge from hurricane
slosh is able to estimate still water surge by grid cell for various hurricane intensity angle of approach to the shoreline forward movement speed and landfall location
additional algorithm are used to model total building damage cost for each grid cell based on and rating curve
hobeika and jamei describe the massevacuation massvac simulation software designed to analyse and evaluate traffic evacuation plan given a natural disaster in an urban area
the system comprises three interrelated module community and disaster type characteristic module population distribution module network evacuation module
the type of natural disaster determines the time period within which the road network ha to be evacuated
the control and management strategy are directly correlated to each specific disaster scenario
massvac is quite flexible and various road network option are available such a traffic signal timing on the road network traffic reserved lane for special vehicle such a those of the emergency service
hobeika and jamei have tested massvac on various evacuation scenario for virginia beach city in order to determine evacuation time for flood and hurricane condition
in general they suggest that the model provided reasonable and reliable evacuation time
southworth et al have enhanced the massvac model with the addition of a colour graphic module which they call mvopl
this module ha been developed using ibm graphic kernel system and provides a number of display screen
the most interesting are those which portray population flow a scaled ribbon on the network diagram and evacuation shelter capacity a bar diagram
the diagram are updated periodically during the course of the simulation
in dry part of the world such a australia forest and bush fire are an important natural hazard and some attention ha been given to the way in which gi might help examine their potential impact
kessell describes a gi called preplan pristine environment planning language which is a natural area management planning and fire modelling system developed for the australian national park and wildlife service preplan comprises four module a simple gi a grid cell resource database a wide range of vegetation fuel fire behaviour erosion and model tabular statistical and colour graphic output system
with this system fire growth can be modelled taking into account change in terrain fuel and temporal change in the weather
kessell point out that uncontrollable fire are recurrent phenomenon in many part of australia causing damage in the hundred of million of dollar and significant loss of life
system such a preplan can provide the user with sound model of the behaviour pattern of fire and are therefore of enormous value in planning
one of the most widespread natural hazard is flooding and the potential for loss of property risk to life and general social disruption is large
one interesting example of a gi approach to flood damage estimation is the anuflood package which wa developed in the early following detailed flood damage study for coastal town in northern new south wale australia smith and greenaway
the anuflood system requires locational and building type data on individual property curve relating the average damage that would result from overfloor flooding to differing depth for each property type and lastly flood frequency in term of flood height expressed a a probability
output from the system is both tabular and graphical
of particular interest is the construction of map showing the expected annual amount of damage for gridded area
anuflood also contains module which permit the investigation of various flood damage mitigation option such a property height raising levee construction and flood proofing
environmental epidemiology
the possibility sketched above relate to emergency planning the search for hazardous site and risk assessment
to what extent can gi help if an event occurs
what for instance of the health consequence
there is a rich tradition of epidemiological work in geography and with the increasing availability of spatially referenced medical data the scope for gi application is wide gatrell
for instance diggle et al ass the hypothesis that cancer of the larynx is associated with proximity to a incinerator and develop a statistical model from the theory of spatial point process to test this
this would have been impossible without the link provided from postcoded data increasingly available from source such a cancer registry to ordnance survey o grid reference
such a link is provided by the central postcode directory which match all million unit postcode in the uk to grid reference
when the case of laryngeal cancer are compared with a null distribution provided by the distribution of much more common lung cancer the hypothesis is given strong support
although the proposed method is novel it is but one of an increasingly large number of method designed to detect and model cluster of disease see for example cuzick and edward
the work of diggle et al examined only a single point source though it generalizes to multiple source and to linear hazard a well
a a second example of health work linked to hazard study we may cite the research being conducted by cross on childhood leukaemia
there are numerous hypothesis concerning the aetiology of this disease from ionizing radiation to viral transmission and cross approach is to collect digital data designed to test some of these hypothesis and to use to display and analyse result
for instance one hypothesis concern the role of electromagnetic radiation a source of which is overhead transmission line a noted earlier
if these are digitized and buffer zone constructed around them fig we can quite easily test hypothesis about prevalence in such buffer zone a compared with prevalence outside
however we should bear in mind the earlier point about the resolution of the data since such electromagnetic effect have a very weak effect beyond perhaps m wertheimer and leeper
there ha been a suspicion for many year that high rate of stomach cancer in part of wale may be linked to soil chemistry specifically such factor a ratio and to lead content in water supply
matthew ha used data from the regional cancer registry morbidity rather than mortality data and data on trace element to examine this link
since the latter are available for a km raster the registration data are assigned to these grid square using the o grid reference
a with any such study there are the usual problem of ecological analysis and influence of migration together with issue of separating out the risk factor under investigation from possible confounding factor
in the usa morrill report on the beginning of a study into the possible radiation dos received a result of radiation release by the hanford washington state nuclear complex would seem to cry out for gi skill to be applied morrill
the research project will employ plume dispersion model in order to model dispersal by wind and will need to integrate this and other environmental data with detailed demographic record
to some extent this line of approach wa anticipated by johnson in his study of exposure to plutonium from the rocky flat nuclear weapon plant near denver see zeigler et al
using soil sample he constructed a contoured risk surface and then mapped excess cancer in various distance band detecting a marked distance decay effect
research problem and prospect
the work reviewed above suggests that the application of gi technique to hazard assessment emergency planning and environmental monitoring is both actually and potentially an important research area with many challenging problem
undoubtedly the gi of the will look very different from their rather primitive ancestor
computer power is becoming cheaper digital data more readily available and gi are becoming hybrid system involving other technology
in this last section we highlight some important research area a we see them
doubtless there are many others such is the surge of interest in gi technology
data availability
we should first consider the availability and quality of data concerning the population who may be at risk from the storage and transport of hazardous substance from toxic air pollution from flooding and so on
such data are crucial either for assisting the emergency service to make assessment about resource they need to deploy in such event or for estimate to be made of risk
within the public domain in the uk we must rely in general on data from the most recent population census the lowest level being that for enumeration district ed
a is well known rhind these contain on average perhaps household and people
the boundary ed have not been widely digitized unlike the electoral ward
however the centroid of ed are available a m grid reference and artificial ed polygon can be created if necessary
in some instance such data will suffice in many case they will have to suffice a nothing better is available
but in some area ed are very extensive physical unit and the shape will be quite distorted
furthermore the scale at which population estimate are often required mean that even ed are too coarse for risk assessment
for instance in performing it quantitative risk assessment the health and safety executive will rarely deal with distance from hazardous site in excess of km petts and census data will not offer sufficient resolution for accurate population estimate to be made
it should be pointed out however that the national radiological protection board currently us km grid square resolution population data from the census in it radiological protection study hallam et al
it would seem that despite the cost involved they should consider investing in the very detailed digital data pinpoint address code pac provided by pinpoint analysis ltd
this area of application would appear to be an obvious market for such a product
a useful research exercise would be to compare the use of census and pac data in deriving quantitative risk assessment and this is an interesting research problem
even with pac data some assumption would need to be made about number of person per household if good population estimate were to be made
more generally we need to consider the availability of large database for hazard study and emergency planning and this is an area ripe for major initiative
in the uk we seem to be lagging well behind the usa in the construction of database on hazardous site and especially hazard event such a those involving toxic release
for instance lioy and daisey in their work on the monitoring of toxic air pollution in new jersey construct what they term a microinventory for each of three town comprising the location of chemical plant metal processing plant paint spray manufacturer and so on
some attribute information is available for these
more closely linked to gi is work by mcmaster and johnson who perform a very detailed inventory of hazardous material both stored and transported in santa monica california
although the raster display are very crude it is simple to answer spatial query concerning the location of people for instance particular age group within certain distance of toxic hazard site
we have data on some hazardous site those regulated by cimah in the uk but a much more comprehensive approach should be adopted especially if we are serious in the search for environmental association with chronic disease
the same is true for toxic release
in the usa the environmental protection agency produce an acute hazard event database while the department of transportation ha a database recording detail of release of toxic material such detail include locational information type and amount of material released mode of release and resulting injury or death cutter and solecki
can we not use gi technology to construct risk mosaic zeigler et al at a variety of spatial scale akin to hewitt and burton hazardousness of a place
in the uk only a handful of county emergency planning department cumbria for instance have built up resource database in digital form and this need to be promoted
further afield we need to recognize that some disaster most obviously chernobyl will have implication for more than one country so that environmental monitoring should take place with some kind of international
there will also be movement of hazardous cargo across frontier and there are clearly problem of risk assessment and planning for emergency at or near international boundary or at sea and airport
a noted above the work of fedra is a major step in this direction and link need to be forged between initiative in the uk and the rest of europe
in term of database on hazardous waste attention ha already been drawn to the waste disposal plan prepared by wras
these give detail of present site location and some indication of permitted waste though little or no information on closed and abandoned site
however for detail of disposal the individual site licence must be consulted
the former hazardous waste inspectorate operated a large database on all site with detail of permitted waste including allowable quantity
the database wa created by a commercial company aspinwall ltd
there are numerous potentially usable database for environmental epidemiological work
opcs of course is a major data repository for medical statistic and their various monitor series are of use though only at the scale of district health authority and above see gatrell and lovett for an example
regional health authority will from time to time produce mortality data at ward level
however if cancer are of interest it is more appropriate to obtain data from regional cancer registry these data are morbidity rather than mortality data and are therefore more valuable
the data are postcoded and may have some occupational detail
for example we have received data from the regional cancer registry in manchester comprising all cancer of the larynx and lung notified between and
this large data set to which grid reference have now been added comprises information about nearly individual
it ha now been copied into ingres a relational database management system permitting query to be made about subset of the data for instance all male between the age of and suffering from laryngeal cancer
other data source on cancer are independent registry of malignancy
an example is that on leukaemia managed by the leukaemia research fund centre in leeds alexander et al
it should be noted that there are frequently major discrepancy between the regional registry and the specialist registry partly because the latter receive notification directly from consultant
indeed working directly with consultant prof invaluable in gaining access to morbidity data
two other potential source of data are worth mentioning
first attention should be drawn to the new directive from the department of health to regional and district health authority to review the health of the population
this mean in practice that district medical officer are charged with preparing an annual report presenting and interpreting epidemiological data identifying local health problem and evaluating service outcome
lancaster university is already heavily involved in the work of preston district health authority in this area
second family health service authority fhsas are also required to take on these role but from the viewpoint of primary health care service
fhsas which correspond to county and to metropolitan borough hold large database on service provided by general practitioner for instance uptake of immunization and screening for breast and cervical cancer
is it we wonder possible to contemplate bringing together some of these data source to form a national online health information system nohis to parallel that for employment and unemployment townsend et al
this might include data on morbidity and mortality uptake of preventative medicine service use and availability at both primary and hospital level
it would be a useful management tool particularly in view of the reorganization taking place in the national health service
it should not be forgotten that hazard themselves have geographical distribution yet there ha been little effort in the uk to develop public domain database
are there area
is there a regional differentiation in hazard type
these are of course commercially important question and a good deal of money is going into the collection of such data by insurance company
one well known database is major hazard incident data service mhidas global industrial hazard database which is currently being developed by the safety and reliability directorate on behalf of the major hazard assessment unit of the uk health and safety directorate
this system currently run in dbase ii and contains in excess of item of professionally assessed information on major hazard coded into some separate field
unfortunately the spatial referencing is poor and with some effort this could easily be remedied
it is for example little use when recording a chemical spill into an egyptian river to have entered into the appropriate field the nile after all this river is some km long
here in our view is a classic case of the absence of a geographical input rendering the data of limited value
in some case good hazard data exist but have simply not yet found their way into a gi
a case in point is inland and coastal flooding
most river authority have detailed map showing the geographical limit of flood in relation to their return period
within the next decade a the privatized water company develop their gi we shall see a massive amount of data conversion in this area
this development together with the availability of digital terrain model will allow quite sophisticated flood forecasting model to be developed within a gi framework
a rise in the next year due to the greenhouse effect this very practical use of gi technology is likely to become commonplace and of considerable practical importance
spatial statistic
another way in which there need to be a rapprochement between statistical method and gi is in the area of spatial sampling and estimation from spatial sample
this is clearly an important issue in radiation monitoring a the discussion of rimnet above implies
a an example peirson ha reviewed the evidence on artificial radioactivity in cumbria and show map of the distribution of certain radionuclides a contoured surface
the point worth making here is that there are many alternative scheme for interpolating from irregular point data lam
one method in particular kriging now available a part of the uniras software offer not only a contoured surface but also an estimate of the standard error at any point on the map
where this is high it suggests that an additional sampling station might be set up
such technique are now standard in environmental science see streit for an application to rainfall monitoring and need to be promoted vigorously in hazard study estes et al
related to this problem is that of making population estimate for new zone that result from overlay operation
we may want to count number living within plume circle of fixed radius buffer zone and so on
existing gi technique usually base the estimate on share so that a new polygon created by slicing an existing area in half is assigned half the population of that source unit
this may be quite absurd in some case notably where population is spatially clustered within a physically large ed
at the nwrrl work is under way flowerdew and green to solve such problem using the em algorithm and the statistical modelling package glim which ha been interfaced with
operation research method and simulation
while there is some research activity in linking statistical model to gi there would seem to be scope for further application of operation research technique to gi problem
within some sophisticated gi such a there are some useful algorithm such a shortest path calculation but gi developer have in general failed to realize the natural link between gi function and many operation research technique
over the last year or so a large theoretical literature ha been developed to provide tool for the solution of many problem associated with emergency planning kolesar
one important class of problem is the selection of location for the emergency service unit
the choice of location need not be for permanent base but can also include dynamic repositioning of unit a circumstance dictate kolesar and walker
in any major emergency a typical problem is the assignment of resource to demand
if resource are held at one set of location and the demand are at another and the cost of transportation are known how do we allocate the resource most efficiently
in a major emergency for example there might be a need to supply blood product held at regional blood bank to hospital
this of course is the classic transportation problem and it solution is well known
a far a we know the emergency response system devised by belardo et al is the only software to incorporate this algorithm
in this system the solution to the transportation problem is shown graphically on the road network which is displayed on the computer screen
a a last example of the potential role of operation research in gi and disaster management we are reminded of the logistic problem that faced the peel regional police force during the mississauga evacuation mentioned previously scanlon and padgham
during the early state of the phased evacuation the logistical problem facing the police wa the warning of the population to make ready for evacuation
speed wa of the essence and manpower wa limited
here then is a familiar operation research network problem all road have to be traversed such that the journey is a minimum
this is the chinese postman problem which provides a hamiltonian circuit through the arc a compared with the travelling salesman problem which is a minimum route through the network node
