task analysis ha not and can not be reduced to a set of standardised procedure which the aspiring analyst could acquire in a formal training course
the technique just described are no more than guideline in what remains the creative art of studying and describing what an experienced worker is doing or will be required to do
the danger in being too rigid is that justice will not be done to the flexibility and complexity of human performance
the danger of being too flexible is that the ergonomists will have an inadequate basis from which to design interface training course and other operator aid
if a comprehensive task description can be completed then it is legitimate to enquire why the task can not be allocated to a technical device rather than a human being
yet without a reasonably comprehensive task description the total system performance may be unreliable or unpredictable
there is a necessary compromise which can only be arrived at in the context of a particular system
a mentioned earlier there are always the twin problem of how to get the information and how to present it
it is sometimes easier to proceed on the basis of if i were doing the job this is how i would do it but this can be delusory even for analyst who have past experience a operator
for analyst who are designer creating a new task there may be no alternative but any task description arrived at by this method should be checked against the behaviour of real operator a they gain experience
a particular difficulty about task synthesis is that there is no easy way of confirming completeness
a task description which is part of a design process should be fully documented in term of the origin of information the assumption made and the method used
the standard method of producing task description is to write all the separate at various level on card and then assemble the card in a network
there is a temptation to make these final diagram very large but often it is more useful to separate into small unit with
the optimum size seems to be this is easily copied and circulated but is large enough to contain considerable detail
the procedure can be computerised there are programme available for the easy production manipulation and storage of block diagram with useful facility
there is an inherent difficulty in that often the main dividend from a task analysis is from the act of obtaining it
those not involved find it difficult to gain very much from a presentation of a task description
like reference book they have to be used rather than read
task analysis can be very expensive in skilled manpower but in looking at it is important to include in value the increase in mutual understanding which occurs when a team conduct the analysis
if such a team is used the required can be optimised by using the delphi method rather than a long series of group meeting
political economic and social issue which arise in conducting task analysis are discussed in the context of job analysis
application
planning
the human resource concept of a the central asset of any organisation ha made some progress over the past twenty year
there wa particular interest around when company were prosperous stable and innovative ipm patten
the objective is to revise and almost reverse the traditional accountancy concept of a a resource consuming factor requiring regular payment overhead in the form of heated lighted equipped workspace and so on
from the narrow accountancy viewpoint people are a cost and it is desirable to keep this cost a low a possible
in these term it is very difficult to justify for example sending a member of staff on a training course
the training requires expenditure and so also doe the replacement for the person away
where is the return
the return is actually in the improved human resource but this is not readily measurable in term which accountant use
there have been two attempt to reduce human resource to this form of measurement giles and robinson
one is to acquire a human asset multiplier for each level of staff
the multiplier for manual staff might be unity but it increase with staff level and becomes three or more for management
the other is to add together all the personnel cost for each kind of worker from the original job advertisement through to the retirement or redundancy payment
the first doe attempt to obtain a value the second remains essentially a cost and not a value
it would be unduly optimistic to assume that management skill have risen to a level such that cost undertaken can be assumed to be equivalent to value
a le direct measure which is applicable only to the most senior management is to observe the fall or rise of the share price when a particular executive leaf or join a company
this can be very high for a large company a change in market value of million of pound is not unusual
the most serious consequence of the accountancy view of is that high level policy doe not give this factor sufficient weight
for example the main board of a company will have complete detail of cost and value of physical resource such a building and equipment but relatively scanty data about the which is their most important asset
indeed it will be described almost entirely a a liability because the cost will be known
similarly broad factor such a the state of morale will again only be described by negative feature such a absenteeism stoppage strike low quality output and so on
it is obvious that company output and project must reflect the and it performance level but if this is acknowledged at all it is only in brief verbal term within for example the chairman annual report
the obsession of current management with measurement and the reduction of every variable to number for ease of computer manipulation ha worsened the situation
unfortunately there is no easy remedy
human resource are too complex a variable to be easily susceptible to measurement beyond the level of counting head and trade
key variable such a the quality of staff at any level and the current morale are only expressible in general verbal descriptive term
it is generally accepted that hygiene type variable such a pay and working condition can if they are inappropriately specified depress morale and motivation but they will not in themselves result in very high level of these parameter
morale and motivation are influenced more by condition of work in the sense of work variety opportunity and attitude of management
these factor are worthy of emphasis because in practice they are still dealt with very badly in many organisation and yet it take little trouble or expertise to make an enormous difference
for example very few senior management take the trouble to keep worker fully informed about policy and likely change
the result is excessive reliance on rumour and continuous speculation which is not only but is also highly deleterious in morale term
the two human factor which can be unambiguously measured are age and sex
the age distribution of a work force is always an interesting and important source of information
for most purpose a rectangular distribution is the most desirable because it provides the appropriate mix of youthful enthusiasm and ageing experience
it also make for regular change a staff retire and are replaced
many distribution show a peak in a particular age group mainly associated with taking on a large number of young people when the organisation wa started or reorganised this is not desirable because it lead to excessive competition for promotion at particular stage
these comment are obviously most relevant for work force where there is little tendency to move out this is characteristic of a surprisingly large number of organisation in european country and in japan but much le so in the
stable work force have their advantage in term of familiarity with the enterprise and it peculiar need but they do result in problem if the market for the product is erratic or otherwise unpredictable
this is particularly so in high technology design and construction of ship aircraft power station and chemical plant where the product unit is large and expensive and the variety of required expertise is extensive
some peak of demand can be dealt with by using consultant but they tend to be expensive and do not always fit well with but important factor such a the favoured style of the organisation
in well ordered system it may be possible to calculate the length of experience required to achieve the required level of expertise in particular topic and compare this with the lead time for particular product requirement
given time available to train new staff it is not necessary to keep more than a nucleus in that particular expertise
on the other hand if there is usually insufficient notice of need it may be necessary to keep staff who have period with little to do between project
it is also desirable to have the possibility of shifting staff between design and operational duty
this not only provides flexibility in the use of it also improves communication
these real difficulty of utilisation are such a to force many organisation to become larger and larger if they are to remain economic
size provides a cushion to the vicissitude of market but it creates other problem
for example difficulty of communication and in particular how to inculcate the feeling within each individual that he and his performance are important to the organisation
this is considered in more detail in chapter
human resource should be fundamental to subject such a ergonomics which are essentially but the concept remains procedurally undeveloped at any level from a continent through country region and company down to particular working system
this is one reason why policy maker never seem to take account fully of the people affected by their decision
the design of procedure
the increased importance of standardised informational support for both machine and operator ha led to the concept of procedure a a separate design issue within a system fig
much of this information can be incorporated in computer program but there is also a need for extensive printed paper for the use of the operator
this take three main form checklist routine and
the terminology in this field is not standardised
software might be restricted a in this book to computer program but it is sometimes used a the generic term to include all source of information
procedure is sometimes used for what are here called routine and sometimes to indicate all the operator information support except software
the situation is further confused when some but not all the operator information support is itself
sometimes the term is used
however whatever the terminology used there is a requirement for design effort
the quality of procedure would be much improved if designer followed some simple table
many document are written on the implicit assumption that the reader is much like the writer in term of expertise and style of thinking
similarly it is assumed that the condition under which the reading will take place are the same a those of writing which are usually a clean office
they may have to be read in the open air in rain and darkness or within a plant under oily cramped poorly lit condition
the user probably ha limited expertise and he may be working under various stress condition
the material on which the information is printed the typeface used the sequence the structure and the format generally should reflect the condition of use easterby and zwaga
all these thing can be achieved if it is acknowledged that all procedure should a validated by user under the normal condition of use
checklist
checklist are used in the mode for routine maintenance and for
they normally take the form of a series of question or statement which the operator us to guide and structure his inspection of the hardware and other system component
the sequence is dictated by the optimal order in which action should be taken for example in starting up an aircraft
there are many situation when the order is of no great consequence for example a safety audit of a new machine and in this latter case some logical structure is needed
a mentioned above the logic of the design may not be the optimal basis if the way the operator think and act is different
baker suggests that four kind of shortcoming emerge when checklist are validated in the real situation
the operator may deviate from the listed procedure because it may require excessive moving about or because he is interrupted by the requirement of other task
systematic use of a checklist often reveals fault in work design such a inadequate access visibility and labelling
the checklist itself may be inconsistent incomplete imprecise or ambiguous
finally the checklist may have reprographic limitation such a inadequate vertical or horizontal structure poor typeface and insufficient linking of requirement description remark and point
the international ergonomics association developed a general ergonomics checklist which is reproduced in edholm
there is a deceptive simplicity about such list which requires extensive effort to ensure a comprehensive but coherent content
the context is of course the context of ergonomics a conceived by the designer of the list
routine
a routine is the most common form of instructional material
the reader is required to follow a series of step which might for example introduce a change in the performance of a complex system
normally routine are single chain of instruction although it is possible to have some conditional branching
each step should be simple and complete in itself preferably with some indication that successful completion ha been achieved for example the appearance or the change of colour of a signal light or the noise of a motor starting or a change of pressure which indicates that there ha been a change in the flow of some material
a mentioned earlier a routine can often be regarded a a written task description
by definition and design intention routine are inflexible
the user is intended to behave exactly according to their instruction
no great skill or intellectual effort is required which is one way of saying that the human operator is being but the purpose of a routine is usually to avoid common human error such a omitting a step or reversing step
in general the value of formal routine is precisely that the operator left to himself will not normally function in such a systematic sequential manner
knowledge text
knowledge is contained in document which may vary from single sheet presentation to large manual
a instructional material it is indirect in that the reader is not necessarily told what to do a in a routine
rather he is informed about the situation and the purpose of informing him is to provide a knowledge base from which he can work out his own action
nevertheless the relevant action remains important and the knowledge provided should be carefully and stringently selected
it is too easy to follow the academic tradition and provide knowledge for it own sake
the need to know criterion is crucial because unless it is applied the operator can be overburdened with unnecessary material
correspondingly the material should be structured in term of how it is most likely to be used
in this context the operator requires a guide for action and not a scientific
it is invariably better to provide material diagrammatically systematically or at least in short paragraph rather than in flowing prose
consider for example how readily information about the relative position of street is available from a map of a town centre rather than a verbal description of all the street
such a map will enable the reader to work out for himself how to get from one location to another within the town
note the enormous flexibility compared with a routine which would tell him only how to get from one particular point to another
a second important difference is that if he miss his place in a routine he will be totally lost whereas if he happens to go in the wrong direction while using a map he is still able to make whatever correction is necessary
however the map doe require more intellectual effort than doe the routine not only in making decision about how to proceed but also in filtering out the required information from the massive irrelevance for a particular task which is equally available
thus one would expect the use of the map to be slower than the use of routine with the human performance being more versatile but le predictable
with representation such a map it remains important to avoid too much homogeneity and provide substructure in the form of main road and key building or other feature such a river
see for example fig
manual which may contain map schematic diagram and other material warrant separate consideration
the design of manual
a manual is usually in the form of a book or booklet which is sent with the hardware from the maker to the customer
it is part of the communication package from the designer to the user
thus it is a particular form of job aid which provides the operator with information on a system and it performance
the standard of manual design ha traditionally been very low for several reason
for this purpose the designer is too familiar with the product and he rarely take the trouble to find out what the user really need to know
often the manual ha to be provided hurriedly at the end of a project when the budget is running out and it is regarded a a tiresome chore still required after the essential design work ha been completed
the problem is particularly acute for computer
manual for car machine tool and so on are poor but at least it is possible to observe the mechanism and their function
most computer operator do not know or wish to know about the mechanism and in any case these are not accessible to vision and manipulation
the computer operator is entirely dependent on the manual at least in the early stage of gaining familiarity with the system and it function
he is usually very badly served although the principle of manual design are well known
for most system the manual is best divided into part a indicated in table
the first part should be a general introduction which orientates the reader towards the system it purpose it functional structure and mode of operation and it performance limit
this should be followed by a separate section on how to set the system up in the first place and how to check that it is working properly
if it is fairly small it may be necessary to describe how to unpack it fix it into position connect it to power supply and start it up
if it is large the emphasis will be on the start up procedure
the section describing the operation of the system should cover not only how the system operates but also how the user can operate it
extensive use of line drawing schematic diagram algorithmic list is desirable and where prose is used this also should be structured into short sentence with meaningful separation into paragraph
the maintenance section should indicate what if anything the operator is expected to do and the symptom which indicate that more specialist maintenance skill are required
table subdivided into can be extremely helpful
part list including description reference number and sometimes drawing are necessary if the user is expected to deal with his own replacement
a standard fault is to assume that the reader is familiar with the jargon which the designer habitually us
a glossary of term and acronym used can be very helpful not only to the reader but also to the writer who is forced to consider carefully how he is using various technical term
finally all manual should end with an index which supplement the table of content at the beginning
attempting to integrate under five
policy in islington
margaret boushel clare debenham lisa dresner and anna gorbach
during the margaret boushel claire debenham lisa dresner and anna gorbach worked in the london borough of islington within social service for child
this chapter is an account of the way they perceived attempt to develop integrated provision for under five and the barrier in attitude and system which were encountered
the first section provides an overview of provision and service in
the next section describes attempt to create a clear policy
the third section look at the faltering progress towards integrated service
the fourth section examines the formidable barrier that were posed by reorganisation of social service local authority cut and the demise of the inner london education authority
the chapter concludes with a mixture of resignation and determination
background service in islington
islington is a inner city london borough with a child population of
in per cent of under five in islington had the use of an facility per cent on a and per cent on a basis
between and provision gradually increased so that by there were child day centre about playgroups and assisted place funded partially or totally by the social service department and and place in nursery school funded by the inner london education authority
the beacon nursery a local mencap project offered care five day per week to child over one year of age categorised a having severe learning difficulty
unlike council day centre playgroups or community nursery the beacon nursery wa free
child were collected from home by special bus and place were available on demand
the beacon had been in existence for many year and in the past had catered for up to thirty child with a wide range of disability and need
by it had half that number on roll
since number at the beacon continued to fall a it wa increasingly seen a a resource for child with severe and multiple disability
in addition the elfreda rathbone organisation a voluntary organisation helping people with learning disability ran a free day nursery in the borough for a small number of child with learning difficulty
some integrated service emerged in the early one playscheme wa developed through a parent initiative and an integrated adventure playground wa established by a voluntary organisation
worker from the integrated playscheme subsequently supported a local special school in integrating under five into a playgroup
in addition to it mainstream school the borough included five special school providing primary and secondary education to child with special need from islington and neighbouring borough one for child with moderate learning difficulty one for child with severe learning difficulty one for child with emotional and behavioural difficulty one for autistic child and one for child with physical disability
in three of these offered nursery place to child from the age of
the child using all of these service came from a wide range of ethnic background though rarely wa this actively and positively reflected in the type of care provided or the ethnic background of their carers
residential unit
by residential service were designed with care in the community in mind but most were based in specialist setting
for example field end house had been open for three year a a specialist unit for child with learning difficulty and wa designed to offer respite round the clock care
parent had fought for this a a local resource to prevent the need for child to be placed in placement far from home
by field end had been joined by another specialist child respite care unit at leigh road
the social service department also provided thirteen and residential unit for child in care by their number had been reduced to eleven none with wheelchair access and only one with any experience of caring for child with learning difficulty
the community health team
the community health team had major responsibility for assessing child and recommending provision
it included physiotherapist occupational and speech therapist doctor psychologist and a specialist health visitor
they were joined in the network by specialist teacher funded by the ilea and based in the special school who visited child at home before they were due to start school
this group of people met on a regular basis to coordinate service and discus professional issue
discussion of service to individual child also took place
this included deciding between day care or school and parent attitude to different option
often a member of the group wa delegated to advise parent on a course of action
the community health team aim wa to ensure a place of treatment for child from the earliest possible age to enable them to develop to their fullest potential
they were however an group operating without directly involving parent and were generally committed to specialist care in the community
they gave support to the beacon and elfreda rathbone nursery and most member saw these setting a the best place to treat child
because of their early contact with parent they often had considerable influence in steering parent towards specialist provision
the special service team
in the early social worker were funded jointly by the ilea and islington social service department to work with child attending two special school and two specialist unit for partially hearing child
these social worker were based in the borough special service team
they all worked with some under five attending the school they covered
they were aware of a number of child who did not have adequate access to resource or support when parent and professional were becoming aware of the possible extent and implication of the disability
when a vacancy arose within this group of social worker in it wa decided to appoint someone specialising in work with under five with special need
this might have had the effect of drawing family into the specialist system at an earlier stage
instead for a number of reason it proved to be a key step in the development of the debate about integration in islington
first the post wa not attached to any specialist institution
there wa an expectation but not a contractual obligation that the postholder would work closely with the beacon nursery
second the worker had an alternative peer group of worker who were key figure in controlling access to all other facility
third the worker wa committed to the idea that treatment of a medical or disabling condition should not take precedence over the child social emotional and cultural need
there wa now a new worker in the network who also made an early relationship with family but who could present a broader choice of day care to parent
attempting an integration policy
the labour council elected in had a a stated policy aim that every child whose parent so wished wa entitled to a place of some sort
this led to the initiation of an review
the review team set up under the auspex of the social service committee included councillor senior departmental management and representative of the child day centre organiser and social worker in it membership
it proposed a network of centre throughout the borough an idea which the worker had been anxious to promote for some time
day care in each area would be organised and coordinated through the child day centre which would also provide information support and resource to parent
the review had made no mention of child with special need
the specialist social worker and another worker with a personal interest in the issue undertook a supplementary review to examine resource for these child
they interviewed parent specialist professional and mainstream worker and they designed a questionnaire which wa completed by worker in a large proportion of mainstream council service and voluntary organisation a well a by some
broadly the survey confirmed that parent of child with special need had not been given a real choice of placement and that they had to fight hard for mainstream provision if this wa their choice
parent wanted to be part of the and did not feel that they were
many commented on lack of information about the range of facility on offer
one woman described how she felt that she wa never given a choice of provision for her son and objected to being told he should be in a specialist nursery for his own good
she fought hard to get him a playgroup place in the group his older brother attended
because the group had known her and her child for some time they agreed to have a go and the placement went ahead
she commented
i had to fight every step of the way for this
no one told me about it and no one wanted him to have it
i knew it wa right for him this is where he learnt to join in and be like other child
it doe matter that he not like them
i know what is right for my child but i not supposed to say
parent also wanted an increased availability of specialist therapy time but wanted it to be used in a more flexible way
some parent were very worried that more integrated setting would lead to lack of attention for child with special need
definition of special need varied widely in the questionnaire response some defining it a child with disability some including child with behavioural and emotional problem and some including child whose first language wa not english
this made the survey difficult to interpret
the finding were documented in a report a place for all our child ccuf and an analysis wa prepared of the practical and bureaucratic problem in gaining an ordinary childcare place for a child with special need with suggestion for how these might be overcome
these idea were informed by a paper which had already been produced by an active member of the local mencap group who had previously tried to generate the debate within the community health service through the mencap committee
the conference a place for all our child
a a result of this work the coordinating committee for under five ccuf an umbrella organisation of statutory and voluntary sector group and individual providing a service to under five decided to organise a conference to look at the issue of integration of special need child within mainstream provision
prior to the conference various group met to produce short contribution to the debate
these included parent worker specialist worker child day centre organiser and playgroups organiser
each of these group came up with a list of proposal which were sent to everyone attending
about people attended the conference held in april
workshop facilitated by the speaker and the conference organising group examined integration policy overcoming practical problem for child in integrated provision and available source of information
the conference made the following recommendation

for a formal universal information system covering local and specialist resource

for child need to be considered with parent and their wish acknowledged and recognised

for employment of extra staff where needed and employment of peripatetic special need worker

for availability of money for equipment toy and adaptation

for enhanced payment to caring for child with special need

for priority status for child with special need in order to facilitate access to ordinary provision

for training facility for staff in ordinary provision specialist provision and

for greater communication and sharing of resource between ordinary and specialist provision

for therapeutic and professional staff to reflect the cultural background of the child and that for all child including those with special need their environment and activity to express a consciousness of the multicultural society in islington
it wa made clear that all of the above area needed funding from health education and social service before they could be implemented
finally it wa felt that unless the attitude of adviser and became more positive towards integration none of the recommendation could be effective
d warfare and crusade
the poet marbod of rennes celebrated in latin the vengeance which would befall a wicked castellan and his troop
the poem highlight two important development the use of force in punishing aristocratic crime the fruit of princely and the increasing significance of in warfare
intellectual claimed a formative influence in the second too john of marmoutier declared that monk from his own monastery had read vegetius de re militari to geoffrey le bel when he wa investing the castle of a rebellious castellan and ascribed his success to their advice on firebomb
but common sense may have been more important than learning in perceiving the vulnerability of most castle to and catapult for even in they were a a rule primitive structure
demanded on the one hand skilled operator and on the other a plentiful supply of unskilled labourer to move the necessary material
this effectively restricted their use to the wealthy and to those whose claim to assistance under the ban wa incontrovertible
equally the improvement in fortification needed to withstand their effect thick stone wall inner a well a outer defence required income greater than those of simple lord
the net effect wa that given dedication prince louis vi geoffrey le bel could subdue rebellious castellans within their own demesne and could build castle of their own which were impregnable to all but lengthy and sustained attack
henry ii castle at chinon where the treasury of anjou wa situated wa the model for it generation with it hall upper chamber tower and curtain walling set on a high point above a strategic crossing of the loire
it could be copied only either by those of nearly equal wealth or by those who could concentrate their resource chiefly on defence prince great bishop or in the south especially town
all others became vulnerable
john of salisbury comment that not only the town but also the fortress of gaul feared henry i of england wa revealing of the new situation
similarly campaigning in the field imposed an increasing financial burden
the treaty between robert ii of flanders and henry i of england renewed by their successor stipulated that each knight supplied to the english king should bring three horse with him this at a time when a horse represented a major investment
then knightly armour grew more elaborate and costly throughout the century
and though some knight might be supplied free by feudal service household one had to be maintained by their lord mercenary one needed pay and those with constituted a regular charge on the treasury
besides away from their home base knight were useless on their own
in open battle and in the plundering expedition that constituted the normal form of aggressive warfare they needed the backing of archer both mounted and on foot and of numerous infantryman
the usual source of supply wa town militia suger mention those of rheims laon soissons etampes and paris in the royal army of
but they might have to be supplemented by mercenary from flanders and the low country where the rapidly expanding population forced large number of young men into military career
in the eye of the faithful these brabanters with their freebooting and lack of discipline after the end of campaign were a dangerous a heretic in frederick barbarossa and louis vii agreed to expel them from their land
their value in battle a shield behind which the knight could shelter before they launched their charge ensured their continued employment by those who could afford them notably henry ii of england
but the hatred they aroused meant that they were liable to be brutally slaughtered if captured afterwards
inevitably therefore war on the grand scale a fought by prince bore little resemblance in practice to the feud of lesser men
the divergence wa sharpened by the application of a theoretical distinction the fruit of augustinian theology amplified a the century went on by canon and roman law reference prince pronounced their campaign just war fought against aggressor with the aim of peace or public war declared by a competent authority in the public interest while they condemned the war of lesser men a infraction of the peace
geoffrey martel had perceived the propaganda potential of public war a early a the mid eleventh century later it enabled henry the liberal of champagne to claim the military service of all lord within his county a reapplication of the carolingian ban
so it could be a powerful weapon
yet the logic of the definition suggested that it would benefit especially king whose competence to declare war could not be impugned thus thibaud of blois failed to persuade the monk of marmoutier that they owed him service when he fought against louis vi they claimed discretion in the matter and in the mighty philip of alsace hesitated to commit to battle the army he had summoned against philip augustus through fear that it rank might melt away
the contrast with the united front louis vi and his troop presented to the emperor henry v in wa marked
a royal banner now bestowed respectability on a cause king war were assumed to be for the sake of peace even when cripplingly expensive and increasingly savage
this go some way to explaining why the complicated campaign within toulouse in the second half of the century were largely fought out under the banner of the angevin aragonese and french king and why the revolt of henry ii son had widespread ramification
the twelfth century wa characterized therefore by fewer but more protracted war which smouldered for long period between short sharp bout of conflict like the war that covered must of the reign of henry i of england and louis vi of france the one inaugurated by the great rebellion of which outlived both louis vii and henry ii or that against catalan claim in the south
into these large number of local conflict were subsumed
the pattern caused problem in that the circumstance which might trigger off renewed fighting were unpredictable yet the moment an opportunity offered prince had to be prepared for invading their enemy there wa no time for lengthy preparation
the usual tactic wa to march troop across the enemy territory plundering and looting to take fortified place if the task wa easy to obtain ally among the lord of the locality and to retreat without fighting a battle if at all possible in effect an application to a wider canvas of the some technique of warfare which had earlier made castellans formidable in the immediate environs of their castle
it necessitated the rapid mobilization of auxiliary to join a core of troop kept constantly at the ready the prince military household which became the linch pin of the system
john of marmoutier life of geoffrey le bel offer a glimpse of how strong bond were created between the prince and his follower within the household and how a high level of training wa maintained at all time
geoffrey wa brought up from infancy with the son of neighbouring angevin lord on whose companionship he relied
when it came time for him to be knighted by henry i in rouen he set off for normandy with a crowd of these young men about him
in rouen the occasion wa celebrated with pomp elaborate dress and a great feast and then the youth all demonstrated their military skill at a grand tournament at which geoffrey naturally won the highest honour
it wa within this kind of environment that chivalry flourished that young men learned to identify their vassalage towards their lord a a symbol of their honour that they debated the relative merit of roland and oliver way of displaying loyalty and that they learned the finer point of jousting
tournament were disapproved of by ecclesiastic for they could be both bloody and dangerous
yet they supplied real need
that of an instruction in the martial art compatible with the maintenance of a prince peace that of an outlet for competitive instinct within the claustrophobic confines of a court and that of display to maintain princely social status
so they flourished everywhere
they offered opportunity for men of skill to acquire great position in the world arnoul of ardres caught the eye of countess ida of boulogne through his exploit and they also conferred lustre on the great geoffrey le bel and philip of alsace were throughout france for their distinguished performance in these show battle
all this formed a background to the first century of crusading and it go some way to explaining the more secular aspect of the magnetism which drew french knight to take up the cross in their thousand
urban ii launching the first crusade at clermont in presented it a a natural evolution of the peace movement warrior were to forget their petty feud and squabble in a campaign to promote the interest of holy church
the war declared by one whose moral authority wa unimpeachable wa to free the eastern church to end muslim guardianship of the holy place to restore jerusalem to it proper state
a prince saw it it wa a just war in the fullest sense of the term those who were slaughtered in it battle were regarded a among the martyr of the church
when raymond of toulouse robert ii of flanders robert curthose stephen of blois and hugh of vermandois responded to the call past and present member of their military household fell almost automatically into rank behind them to test themselves against terrible danger but also to enjoy the companionship in arm the adventure the deed of daring which were the stuff of the chansons de geste

the defocusing of an electron beam j e d p h b
we have so far talked about positive and negative charge about point charge and distributed charge

in the present section we shall consider a cylindrical electron beam of radius a in which the charge density is uniform p po and all electron travel with velocity v

the electric force on an electron of charge e travelling at the edge of the beam r a is it is in the radial direction pointing outwards

using a technical term borrowed from electron optic we could say that the electron beam get defocused
the other conclusion a far a it is permissible to generalize from a single example is more important in principle
it is concerned with the relative magnitude of electric and magnetic force

why is it then that we have no difficulty in practice in observing magnetic field
the reason is of course that there are two kind of electric charge and their effect usually cancel so the small magnetic field ha a chance of getting observed

pinch effect j h b

what happens then
if everything wa uniform then the beam diameter would go on decreasing

nevertheless a few qualitative conclusion may be drawn without doing any further mathematics
if the happens to be smaller at a certain place then the force are larger there than at the neighbouring so the beam will be further constricted etc leading to the sausage instability fig a
if the magnetic field happens to be larger at one side than at the other side then the beam will be deflected towards the weaker field which make the field even weaker etc leading to the kink instability fig b
the positive particle is immobile
in practice this mean that the positive ion are part of the crystal lattice
there is then no magnetic force on the ion only on the electron
so the electron want to move inwards but can not because the ion hold them back by virtue of their electrostatic attraction
naturally if the ion attract the electron the converse is true a well owing to the magnetic force on the electron there is also an inward force upon the ion
so the whole crystal structure try to contract or in other word the material is under pressure see example
in any practical situation this pressure is small and can be neglected when calculating the force on conductor

flow pattern and ohm law j e d
up to now we have not enquired into the question of how the current arose
we just assumed that certain charge carrier moved with certain velocity
now we shall say that in a class of material the current density at any point is proportional to the electric field in mathematical form formula where formula is the conductivity of the material
the above equation is spite of it utmost simplicity represents an extremely good guess
it is valid for nearly all material up to quite high electric field
will there be a magnetic field
yes of course whenever there is a current there is a magnetic field a well
but the effect of the magnetic field upon the motion of the electron is nearly always negligible one exception causing the pinch effect is mentioned in the previous section
thus we may safely ignore the magnetic field when determining the line of current flow
we are then left with only one equation formula or formula or formula depending on our preference
eqn tell u that there is some analogy see example with the electrostatic case treated in chapter
we may in fact reinterpret any of the diagram of fig by assuming that the whole space is filled with a material of conductivity formula and the field line are now the line of current flow a well
is the analogy perfect
not really because a current flow there is some potential drop in the electrode itself zero conductivity for part of the space can not be electrostatically modelled since there are no dielectric with er and when current flow through two material of different conductivity there is generally a surface charge at the boundary see example
it is not worth discussing any of these complication because one is rarely called upon to work out line of current in a conductor
we shall rather return to a very simple geometrical configuration for deriving ohm law
we shall take a piece of cylindrical material of length l and s and apply a voltage between the end
the electric field is then formula the current density formula and the current formula
from circuit theory formula where r is the resistance of the material
comparing eqns and we get formula
since formula is by definition the resistivity we get the result you learned in school that the electrical resistance is proportional to the resistivity and the length of the sample and inversely proportional to it
a more general definition of resistance valid for varying may be easily arrived at but it is hardly worth the trouble
the essential thing is that the relation formula is equivalent to ohm law
risking the dismay of circuit engineer some theoretician do in fact refer to eqn a ohm law
